Teaches a design-system-agnostic method: a form heuristic, a color formula with a runnable validator, mark specs, and interaction rules. A validated default palette is documented in `references/palette.md` — swap that file's values for your brand's. Triggers on: \"chart\", \"graph\", \"plot\", \"data viz\", \"visualization\", \"dashboard\", \"analytics\", \"visualize data\", \"categorical colors\", \"sequential / diverging palette\", \"stat tile\", \"sparkline\", \"heatmap\", \"legend\", \"axis\", \"tooltip\", \"chart colors\", \"color by series\".\n- artifact-design: Design guidance and fundamentals for Artifacts.\n- update-config: Use this skill to configure the Claude Code harness via settings.json. Automated behaviors (\"from now on when X\", \"each time X\", \"whenever X\", \"before/after X\") require hooks configured in settings.json - the harness executes these, not Claude, so memory/preferences cannot fulfill them. Also use for: permissions (\"allow X\", \"add permission\", \"move permission to\"), env vars (\"set X=Y\"), hook troubleshooting, or any changes to settings.json/settings.local.json files. Examples: \"allow npm commands\", \"add bq permission to global settings\", \"move permission to user settings\", \"set DEBUG=true\", \"when claude stops show X\". For simple settings like theme/model, suggest the /config command.\n- keybindings-help: Use when the user wants to customize keyboard shortcuts, rebind keys, add chord bindings, or modify ~/.claude/keybindings.json. Examples: \"rebind ctrl+s\", \"add a chord shortcut\", \"change the submit key\", \"customize keybindings\".\n- verify: Verify that a code change actually does what it's supposed to by exercising it end-to-end and observing behavior — drive the affected flow, not just tests or typecheck. Run before committing nontrivial changes; bootstraps this repo's project verify skill if none exists yet. Don't invoke it on a diff that only touches tests, docs, or other code with no runtime surface to drive (a change to product source always has one) — there's nothing to observe.\n- code-review: Review the current diff for correctness bugs and reuse/simplification/efficiency cleanups at the given effort level (low/medium: fewer, high-confidence findings; high→max: broader coverage, may include uncertain findings; ultra: deep multi-agent review in the cloud). Pass --comment to post findings as inline PR comments, or --fix to apply the findings to the working tree after the review.\n- simplify: Review the changed code for reuse, simplification, efficiency, and altitude cleanups, then apply the fixes. Quality only — it does not hunt for bugs; use /code-review for that.\n- fewer-permission-prompts: Scan your transcripts for common read-only Bash and MCP tool calls, then add a prioritized allowlist to project .claude/settings.json to reduce permission prompts.\n- loop: Run a prompt or slash command on a recurring interval (e.g. /loop 5m /foo). Omit the interval to let the model self-pace. - When the user wants to set up a recurring task, poll for status, or run something repeatedly on an interval (e.g. \"check the deploy every 5 minutes\", \"keep running /babysit-prs\"). Do NOT invoke for one-off tasks.\n- schedule: Create, update, list, or run scheduled cloud agents (routines) that execute on a cron schedule. - When the user wants to schedule a recurring cloud agent, set up automated tasks, create a cron job for Claude Code, or manage their scheduled agents/routines. Also use when the user wants a one-time scheduled run (\"run this once at 3pm\", \"remind me to check X tomorrow\").\n- claude-api: Reference for the Claude API / Anthropic SDK — model ids, pricing, params, streaming, tool use, MCP, agents, caching, token counting, model migration.\nTRIGGER — read BEFORE opening the target file; don't skip because it \"looks like a one-liner\" — whenever: the prompt names Claude/Anthropic in any form (Claude, Anthropic, Fable, Opus, Sonnet, Haiku, `anthropic`, `@anthropic-ai`, `claude-*`, `us.anthropic.*`, `[1m]`); the user asks about an LLM (pricing/model choice/limits/caching) — never answer from memory; OR the task is LLM-shaped with provider unstated (agent/MCP/tool-definition/multi-agent/RAG/LLM-judge/computer-use; generate/summarize/extract/classify/rewrite/converse over NL; debugging refusals/cutoffs/streaming/tool-calls/tokens).\nSKIP only when another provider is being worked on (overrides all triggers): OpenAI/GPT/Gemini/Llama/Mistral/Cohere/Ollama named in the query; OR `grep -rE 'openai|langchain_openai|google.generativeai|genai|mistralai|cohere|ollama'` over the project hits (run this grep FIRST if no provider named — don't Read the file).\n- run: Launch and drive this project's app to see a change working. {"parentUuid":"b7460f42-3bb7-4bb7-b834-6e28229b1dec","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"38bde3ab-a47f-4b91-886b-2dfe1e9b27d1","agentId":"ab5a61a500485d254","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_0181oC7YLqkha5gx2U2dbwgs","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# Audit: live-play animation integration (2026-07-07)\n2\t\n3\tScope: the four symptoms from tonight's Self-vs-copycat-v0 game, plus a fit\n4\treview of the animation backbone's live-play integration. Replay mode is not\n5\tin question — it follows `docs/replay-animation-architecture.md` and is well\n6\ttested. Live play is where the seams are.\n7\t\n8\t## Executive summary\n9\t\n10\tLive play violates the architecture's core premise in two ways. First, event\n11\tidentity is broken: the engine delivers per-player *delta* logs, so the same\n12\tlog lines arrive twice (once per perspective), and `localEngine.appendTimeline`\n13\tassigns fresh ids on every arrival (`localEngine.ts:490-492`) — the gate\n14\ttracks *ids*, not content, so every actor switch re-animates the previous\n15\tturn. Measured empirically through the bridge: on the agent's first\n16\tobservation after a human action, **12 of 13 logs were duplicates** of\n17\talready-delivered lines. Second, live feeds the animation backbone cumulative\n18\ttimelines against final board state (Step playback defaults off,\n19\t`viewSettings.svelte.ts:43`), while everything downstream was designed for\n20\treplay's per-phase projected views. The scattered live-only patches —\n21\t`knownHands`, synthesized playback prompts, agent-view filtering, the\n22\tsequence stepping loop — are compensations for that mismatch, and they leak\n23\t(placeholder hands without serials break anchors; hide claims land on\n24\ttop-of-pile fallbacks). Root fix: give live play the same per-action phase\n25\tcontract replay already has, and delete the patches.\n26\t\n27\t## Symptom diagnoses\n28\t\n29\t### 1. \"After my turn finishes, the whole turn re-animates\"\n30\t\n31\t**Root cause: duplicate logs re-enter the timeline with new ids.**\n32\t\n33\tThe engine's observations carry logs since *that actor's* last observation.\n34\tWhen the turn passes to the agent, the agent's first observation re-contains\n35\tthe human turn's logs. Probe through the real bridge (first-legal agent,\n36\thydrapple mirror):\n37\t\n38\t```\n39\tstep3: actor=1 logs=17 dupes_of_earlier=2\n40\tstep5: actor=1 logs=13 dupes_of_earlier=12   <- agent obs re-delivers human turn\n41\t```\n42\t\n43\t`appendTimeline` converts every observation's logs with a fresh id range\n44\t(`localEngine.ts:489-492`, `cabtLogsToTimeline(logs, { nextId: this.timelineId })`)\n45\tand appends to the cumulative `actionTimeline`. `AnimationEventGate` batches\n46\t\"unseen\" events by **id** (`gate.ts:37-41`, `timing.ts:39-40`), so re-id'd\n47\tduplicates always animate. Every actor switch therefore replays the prior\n48\tturn's motions. This is the primary driver of symptoms 3 and 4 as well.\n49\t\n50\t### 2. \"Opponent's hand count wouldn't fully update\"\n51\t\n52\t**Root cause: perspective-flipping views plus re-fired draw animations\n53\tclaiming hand slots.**\n54\t\n55\tLive sequence views are built from whichever player's perspective the engine\n56\tobservation happens to be (`demoEngine.ts:436-437`: `activePlayerIndex =\n57\tcurrent.yourIndex`; hands render from `player.hand` when present, otherwise\n58\t`handCount` placeholder card backs, `demoEngine.ts:463-466`). During the agent's\n59\tturn the human-perspective hand data goes stale; `withKnownHands`\n60\t(`localEngine.ts:457-483`) patches a hand back in **only when the remembered\n61\thand length equals the current `handCount`** — exactly the interesting moments\n62\t(draw, prize to hand, discard from hand) fail the check and fall back to\n63\tserial-less placeholders. Meanwhile each re-fired duplicate draw batch claims\n64\thand-slot elements with mode `element` for the animation window\n65\t(`ViewportAnimationLayer.svelte:483-575`, `claim(target)` per draw), hiding\n66\treal card backs while sprites fly again. Net effect: the opponent's hand\n67\tvisually lags or under-counts until claims release and a fresh\n68\tcorrect-perspective observation arrives.\n69\t\n70\t### 3. \"Prize cards I drew were hidden until the next turn, then re-drawn\"\n71\t\n72\t**Root cause: per-player log delivery delays the prize-take event, and the\n73\tknownHands length check hides the card meanwhile; the duplicate then\n74\tre-animates it.**\n75\t\n76\tA KO + prize-take usually happens on the attack that ends your turn, so those\n77\tlogs first arrive in the *agent's* observation (per-player delta). For the\n78\twhole opponent turn, views of your hand come from `withKnownHands` — but your\n79\t`handCount` grew by the prize card, the length check fails\n80\t(`localEngine.ts:470-472`), and your hand renders placeholders/stale content\n81\twithout the prize card. When your next observation finally arrives with the\n82\tsame logs again (duplicate), the prize-take animates a second time\n83\t(`ViewportAnimationLayer.svelte:645-737`) — the \"re-drawn next turn\" you saw.\n84\t`prizeSourceRects`/`takeIndex` extrapolation happily animates from already-empty\n85\tprize slots, which is correct for replay but masks the duplication here.\n86\t\n87\t### 4. \"Opponent's discard pile constantly went blank\"\n88\t\n89\t**Root cause: re-fired KO/discard/mill animations repeatedly hide the pile's\n90\ttop card (or the pile), because live cards have no serials and discard anchors\n91\tdegrade to coarse fallbacks.**\n92\t\n93\tLive observations carry no `serial` on cards (serials are synthesized by the\n94\treplay pipeline; the bridge's raw player objects have none — verified against\n95\ta live bridge session). Discard motions hide\n96\t`{ kind: 'discard', exact: true, serial, cardId }` (`motions.ts:544-546,\n97\t582-584`); with `serial` undefined, `discardCardElement` matches **by cardId**\n98\t(`anchors.ts:136+`) — any copy, usually the top card — and non-exact discard\n99\tanchors fall back exact → top card → whole pile (`anchors.ts:54-61`). Combine\n100\twith symptom 1's re-fire storm: every actor switch re-claims the discard's\n101\ttop card / pile element for the duration of a KO-or-mill animation, and a\n102\tsmall pile reads as blank over and over. `RevealSessionLayer` adds to this\n103\tduring search-heavy turns (hydrapple!): its scope-change session clearing is\n104\treplay-gated (`RevealSessionLayer.svelte:82`), so live sessions and their\n105\t`contents` claims can linger until the next reveal batch.\n106\t\n107\t## What fits well\n108\t\n109\t- **The visibility manager** (`visibility.ts`): single attribute, ref-counted\n110\t  claims, one owner. Nothing else in the codebase hides cards. This is the\n111\t  strongest invariant and it held up under audit.\n112\t- **Semantic anchors with fallback chains** (`anchors.ts`): the design is\n113\t  right; live's problems are missing *data* (serials), not the resolver.\n114\t- **The motion contract + choreograph as pure classifier** (`motions.ts`):\n115\t  clean separation; layers don't classify events, tests cover grouping.\n116\t- **The gate as a concept** (`gate.ts`): 40 lines, one job, honestly\n117\t  documented. It does exactly what it promises — the inputs betray it.\n118\t- **Replay's phase pipeline** (`cabtReplay.ts` + projected phase views):\n119\t  the architecture doc's contract is real and tested (3.8k lines of tests).\n120\t- **Board/viewport layer split** and cross-plane projection: no coordinate\n121\t  system leaks found.\n122\t\n123\t## What doesn't fit (ranked)\n124\t\n125\t1. **Event identity is positional, not semantic** (`localEngine.ts:489-492`).\n126\t   Ids are assigned per arrival with no dedupe, while the engine's delivery\n127\t   is per-player and overlapping. This single mismatch produces most of what\n128\t   you saw. The gate's \"unseen tail\" premise requires stable identity.\n129\t2. **Live's data shape contradicts the backbone's contract.** Replay: each\n130\t   phase = its own events + a projected view of the board *as it should look\n131\t   during that phase*. Live: cumulative timeline + already-final board, one\n132\t   burst (Step playback off is the default — `viewSettings.svelte.ts:43`).\n133\t   Anchors then resolve against end-state DOM; sources have often already\n134\t   vanished; claims attach to whatever the fallback chain finds.\n135\t3. **The \"one live adapter\" claim is no longer true.** Beyond the gate,\n136\t   live-only compensations live in four places: `withKnownHands`\n137\t   (`localEngine.ts:457`), `revealPromptForLogs` synthesized prompts\n138\t   (`localEngine.ts:522`, with collision-prone `id: -this.timelineId`),\n139\t   `isAgentDecisionView` filtering (`localEngine.ts:513`), and the\n140\t   sequence-stepping loop with fixed delays in `gameStore.apply`\n141\t   (`game.svelte.ts:66-93`). Each is a patch over the data-shape mismatch.\n142\t4. **Perspective mixing.** Views inherit the observation's `yourIndex` as\n143\t   `activePlayerIndex` and hand visibility (`demoEngine.ts:436`), so live\n144\t   sequence views alternate perspective mid-turn. The viewer has a fixed seat;\n145\t   the view builder should too. `knownHands` exists only because of this.\n146\t5. **Serial-less live cards.** Replay synthesizes stable serials; live never\n147\t   did. Exact-card anchors, hand-slot-by-serial, attached-card anchors all\n148\t   silently degrade in live mode.\n149\t6. **Old prompt/selection layer is logically sound but visually parallel.**\n150\t   `promptSelectionModel.ts` / `setupSelectionModel.ts` are small, tested,\n151\t   pure models (good). But playback-only prompts synthesized from log\n152\t   patterns (`revealPromptForLogs`) duplicate what `RevealSessionLayer`\n153\t   already animates — two systems now own \"show milled/revealed cards\",\n154\t   violating the \"exactly one system animates an event\" invariant.\n155\t\n156\t## Recommended path\n157\t\n158\t**Unify live on the phase contract instead of patching the cumulative path.**\n159\tThe local engine already receives per-decision observations (`autoSteps`);\n160\tthose are natural phase boundaries. The shape:\n161\t\n162\t1. **Stable event identity at the source.** In `appendTimeline`, dedupe\n163\t   incoming logs against a content-keyed cursor (the engine gives no log ids,\n164\t   so key on the serialized log + a monotonic per-game sequence that tolerates\n165\t   the per-player overlap). Duplicates get dropped, not re-id'd.\n166\t2. **A live step builder** that turns each observation's *new* logs into a\n167\t   step `{ events, view }` — the view being the board state *at that\n168\t   observation*, seat-fixed to the viewer (always render from the human's\n169\t   seat; opponent hand from `handCount`, own hand from the last own-perspective\n170\t   observation — this replaces `withKnownHands` with an explicit rule instead\n171\t   of a length heuristic). Synthesize serials the way the replay pipeline\n172\t   does, so anchors regain precision.\n173\t3. **Play steps through the same machinery replay uses** (the stepper in\n174\t   `gameStore.apply` becomes the one consumer; `animateActions` stops being a\n175\t   correctness switch and becomes pacing only). The gate keeps its replay\n176\t   scope behavior; its live \"unseen tail\" mode shrinks to a no-op and can be\n177\t   deleted.\n178\t4. **Delete the compensations**: `withKnownHands`, `revealPromptForLogs` (the\n179\t   reveal session layer already owns that animation), `isAgentDecisionView`\n180\t   filtering (the step builder simply doesn't emit steps for agent decision\n181\t   points).\n182\t\n183\tThis is a few focused days, mostly in `localEngine.ts`, reusing grouping\n184\tlogic from `cabtReplay.ts` rather than duplicating it. It removes code on\n185\tnet and makes live/replay share one honest contract, which is the\n186\tsimplification you asked for.\n187\t\n188\t| Old piece | Verdict | Note |\n189\t|---|---|---|\n190\t| `AnimationEventGate` live mode | **Replace** | Phase steps make \"unseen tail\" unnecessary; keep replay scope logic |\n191\t| `gameStore.apply` sequence loop (`game.svelte.ts:66`) | **Adapt** | Becomes the single step player for live phases; delays → pacing only |\n192\t| `withKnownHands` (`localEngine.ts:457`) | **Replace** | Seat-fixed view builder with explicit own-hand rule |\n193\t| `revealPromptForLogs` (`localEngine.ts:522`) | **Delete** | RevealSessionLayer owns reveal animation; prompt duplicated it |\n194\t| `isAgentDecisionView` (`localEngine.ts:513`) | **Delete** | Step builder emits no step for agent decision points |\n195\t| `promptSelectionModel` / `setupSelectionModel` | **Keep** | Pure, tested input models; restyle later if desired |\n196\t| `cabtLogsToTimeline` (`logFormat.ts`) | **Adapt** | Add content-keyed identity + dedupe cursor |\n197\t| Anchors / visibility / choreograph / layers | **Keep** | Feed them correct data; they already behave |\n198\t\n199\t## Quick fixes (status as of 2026-07-07 evening)\n200\t\n201\t1. **IMPLEMENTED — log dedupe.** `src/engine/logDedupe.ts` (content-signature\n202\t   sliding window, 300 entries) filters every observation's logs in\n203\t   `appendTimeline` before `cabtLogsToTimeline`; the deduper resets with the\n204\t   session. Unit tests in `src/engine/logDedupe.test.ts`. Verified against a\n205\t   live bridge session: 39 of 90 delivered logs were re-deliveries and all\n206\t   were dropped, including the actor-switch observations behind symptom 1\n207\t   (worst case raw=13 → kept=3).\n208\t2. **IMPLEMENTED — turn-boundary claim release.** All three animation layers\n209\t   take a `turnKey` prop (`turn-${game.turn}` in live, constant in replay)\n210\t   and run `endScope()` / `clearSession()` when it changes, so no claim,\n211\t   sprite, or reveal session outlives the turn that created it.\n212\t3. **IMPLEMENTED — Step playback defaults ON** (`viewSettings.svelte.ts`), so\n213\t   live events animate against each intermediate view instead of one burst\n214\t   against the final board.\n215\t4. **IMPLEMENTED — live reveal-session clearing** via the same `turnKey`\n216\t   boundary in `RevealSessionLayer` (replay behavior unchanged; sessions that\n217\t   continue into the incoming batch still survive the boundary).\n218\t5. **IMPLEMENTED — animation-gated sequential playback** (follow-up to the\n219\t   fixed-cadence problem: agent actions overlapped into garbled animations).\n220\t   `src/lib/anim/activity.ts` is a shared busy-until signal: when a layer\n221\t   schedules a live batch it reports the batch's scheduled end\n222\t   (`scheduledEndMs` + handoff/settle padding), and `gameStore.apply` awaits\n223\t   idle before applying the next sequence view (and before the first view of\n224\t   a new response). \"Step ms\" is now the *minimum gap between views*, not the\n225\t   cadence; per-step waits are capped at 5s so a stuck destination poll can't\n226\t   deadlock playback. Playback-prompt confirms are unchanged. Replay pacing\n227\t   untouched (it never consults the signal). Note this is interim mechanics:\n228\t   the structural live-step builder below subsumes it — once live produces\n229\t   proper phases with durations, the stepper can pace from phase metadata the\n230\t   way replay does, and the busy-signal becomes a safety net only.\n231\t\n232\t### Still outstanding\n233\t\n234\t- **Dev overlay for stuck hides**: `animVisibility.hiddenCount()` already\n235\t  exists; surface it in the debug settings panel to catch claim leaks early.\n236\t- **Dedupe caveat** and **the \"Recommended path\" section above** —\n237\t  **LANDED same day.** The seat-fixed live step builder shipped\n238\t  (`src/engine/liveSteps.ts` + reworked `localEngine.appendSteps`), with\n239\t  positional per-seat-stream dedupe instead of content dedupe (it pairs the\n240\t  perspective-variant draws this caveat worried about — measured at roughly\n241\t  one variant pair per draw, not \"occasional\"). `withKnownHands`,\n242\t  `revealPromptForLogs`, `isAgentDecisionView`, `logDedupe`, and the gate's\n243\t  live mode are deleted. Details and divergences:\n244\t  `docs/audit-2026-07-07-viewer-play-pipeline.md`, \"Implementation\n245\t  addendum\". One correction to this document: live observations do carry\n246\t  card serials on known cards (probe-verified); only hidden hand cards\n247\t  needed synthesized identity.\n248\t"}]},"uuid":"af51d204-1863-4d6e-94ca-0bdcc5de4319","timestamp":"2026-07-09T03:07:10.568Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/Users/charlielockyer/Documents/Code/ai-battle-challenge/cabt-viewer/docs/audit-2026-07-07-live-play-animation.md","content":"# Audit: live-play animation integration (2026-07-07)\n\nScope: the four symptoms from tonight's Self-vs-copycat-v0 game, plus a fit\nreview of the animation backbone's live-play integration. Replay mode is not\nin question — it follows `docs/replay-animation-architecture.md` and is well\ntested. Live play is where the seams are.\n\n## Executive summary\n\nLive play violates the architecture's core premise in two ways. First, event\nidentity is broken: the engine delivers per-player *delta* logs, so the same\nlog lines arrive twice (once per perspective), and `localEngine.appendTimeline`\nassigns fresh ids on every arrival (`localEngine.ts:490-492`) — the gate\ntracks *ids*, not content, so every actor switch re-animates the previous\nturn. Measured empirically through the bridge: on the agent's first\nobservation after a human action, **12 of 13 logs were duplicates** of\nalready-delivered lines. Second, live feeds the animation backbone cumulative\ntimelines against final board state (Step playback defaults off,\n`viewSettings.svelte.ts:43`), while everything downstream was designed for\nreplay's per-phase projected views. The scattered live-only patches —\n`knownHands`, synthesized playback prompts, agent-view filtering, the\nsequence stepping loop — are compensations for that mismatch, and they leak\n(placeholder hands without serials break anchors; hide claims land on\ntop-of-pile fallbacks). Root fix: give live play the same per-action phase\ncontract replay already has, and delete the patches.\n\n## Symptom diagnoses\n\n### 1. \"After my turn finishes, the whole turn re-animates\"\n\n**Root cause: duplicate logs re-enter the timeline with new ids.**\n\nThe engine's observations carry logs since *that actor's* last observation.\nWhen the turn passes to the agent, the agent's first observation re-contains\nthe human turn's logs. Probe through the real bridge (first-legal agent,\nhydrapple mirror):\n\n```\nstep3: actor=1 logs=17 dupes_of_earlier=2\nstep5: actor=1 logs=13 dupes_of_earlier=12   <- agent obs re-delivers human turn\n```\n\n`appendTimeline` converts every observation's logs with a fresh id range\n(`localEngine.ts:489-492`, `cabtLogsToTimeline(logs, { nextId: this.timelineId })`)\nand appends to the cumulative `actionTimeline`. `AnimationEventGate` batches\n\"unseen\" events by **id** (`gate.ts:37-41`, `timing.ts:39-40`), so re-id'd\nduplicates always animate. Every actor switch therefore replays the prior\nturn's motions. This is the primary driver of symptoms 3 and 4 as well.\n\n### 2. \"Opponent's hand count wouldn't fully update\"\n\n**Root cause: perspective-flipping views plus re-fired draw animations\nclaiming hand slots.**\n\nLive sequence views are built from whichever player's perspective the engine\nobservation happens to be (`demoEngine.ts:436-437`: `activePlayerIndex =\ncurrent.yourIndex`; hands render from `player.hand` when present, otherwise\n`handCount` placeholder card backs, `demoEngine.ts:463-466`). During the agent's\nturn the human-perspective hand data goes stale; `withKnownHands`\n(`localEngine.ts:457-483`) patches a hand back in **only when the remembered\nhand length equals the current `handCount`** — exactly the interesting moments\n(draw, prize to hand, discard from hand) fail the check and fall back to\nserial-less placeholders. Meanwhile each re-fired duplicate draw batch claims\nhand-slot elements with mode `element` for the animation window\n(`ViewportAnimationLayer.svelte:483-575`, `claim(target)` per draw), hiding\nreal card backs while sprites fly again. Net effect: the opponent's hand\nvisually lags or under-counts until claims release and a fresh\ncorrect-perspective observation arrives.\n\n### 3. \"Prize cards I drew were hidden until the next turn, then re-drawn\"\n\n**Root cause: per-player log delivery delays the prize-take event, and the\nknownHands length check hides the card meanwhile; the duplicate then\nre-animates it.**\n\nA KO + prize-take usually happens on the attack that ends your turn, so those\nlogs first arrive in the *agent's* observation (per-player delta). For the\nwhole opponent turn, views of your hand come from `withKnownHands` — but your\n`handCount` grew by the prize card, the length check fails\n(`localEngine.ts:470-472`), and your hand renders placeholders/stale content\nwithout the prize card. When your next observation finally arrives with the\nsame logs again (duplicate), the prize-take animates a second time\n(`ViewportAnimationLayer.svelte:645-737`) — the \"re-drawn next turn\" you saw.\n`prizeSourceRects`/`takeIndex` extrapolation happily animates from already-empty\nprize slots, which is correct for replay but masks the duplication here.\n\n### 4. \"Opponent's discard pile constantly went blank\"\n\n**Root cause: re-fired KO/discard/mill animations repeatedly hide the pile's\ntop card (or the pile), because live cards have no serials and discard anchors\ndegrade to coarse fallbacks.**\n\nLive observations carry no `serial` on cards (serials are synthesized by the\nreplay pipeline; the bridge's raw player objects have none — verified against\na live bridge session). Discard motions hide\n`{ kind: 'discard', exact: true, serial, cardId }` (`motions.ts:544-546,\n582-584`); with `serial` undefined, `discardCardElement` matches **by cardId**\n(`anchors.ts:136+`) — any copy, usually the top card — and non-exact discard\nanchors fall back exact → top card → whole pile (`anchors.ts:54-61`). Combine\nwith symptom 1's re-fire storm: every actor switch re-claims the discard's\ntop card / pile element for the duration of a KO-or-mill animation, and a\nsmall pile reads as blank over and over. `RevealSessionLayer` adds to this\nduring search-heavy turns (hydrapple!): its scope-change session clearing is\nreplay-gated (`RevealSessionLayer.svelte:82`), so live sessions and their\n`contents` claims can linger until the next reveal batch.\n\n## What fits well\n\n- **The visibility manager** (`visibility.ts`): single attribute, ref-counted\n  claims, one owner. Nothing else in the codebase hides cards. This is the\n  strongest invariant and it held up under audit.\n- **Semantic anchors with fallback chains** (`anchors.ts`): the design is\n  right; live's problems are missing *data* (serials), not the resolver.\n- **The motion contract + choreograph as pure classifier** (`motions.ts`):\n  clean separation; layers don't classify events, tests cover grouping.\n- **The gate as a concept** (`gate.ts`): 40 lines, one job, honestly\n  documented. It does exactly what it promises — the inputs betray it.\n- **Replay's phase pipeline** (`cabtReplay.ts` + projected phase views):\n  the architecture doc's contract is real and tested (3.8k lines of tests).\n- **Board/viewport layer split** and cross-plane projection: no coordinate\n  system leaks found.\n\n## What doesn't fit (ranked)\n\n1. **Event identity is positional, not semantic** (`localEngine.ts:489-492`).\n   Ids are assigned per arrival with no dedupe, while the engine's delivery\n   is per-player and overlapping. This single mismatch produces most of what\n   you saw. The gate's \"unseen tail\" premise requires stable identity.\n2. **Live's data shape contradicts the backbone's contract.** Replay: each\n   phase = its own events + a projected view of the board *as it should look\n   during that phase*. Live: cumulative timeline + already-final board, one\n   burst (Step playback off is the default — `viewSettings.svelte.ts:43`).\n   Anchors then resolve against end-state DOM; sources have often already\n   vanished; claims attach to whatever the fallback chain finds.\n3. **The \"one live adapter\" claim is no longer true.** Beyond the gate,\n   live-only compensations live in four places: `withKnownHands`\n   (`localEngine.ts:457`), `revealPromptForLogs` synthesized prompts\n   (`localEngine.ts:522`, with collision-prone `id: -this.timelineId`),\n   `isAgentDecisionView` filtering (`localEngine.ts:513`), and the\n   sequence-stepping loop with fixed delays in `gameStore.apply`\n   (`game.svelte.ts:66-93`). Each is a patch over the data-shape mismatch.\n4. **Perspective mixing.** Views inherit the observation's `yourIndex` as\n   `activePlayerIndex` and hand visibility (`demoEngine.ts:436`), so live\n   sequence views alternate perspective mid-turn. The viewer has a fixed seat;\n   the view builder should too. `knownHands` exists only because of this.\n5. **Serial-less live cards.** Replay synthesizes stable serials; live never\n   did. Exact-card anchors, hand-slot-by-serial, attached-card anchors all\n   silently degrade in live mode.\n6. **Old prompt/selection layer is logically sound but visually parallel.**\n   `promptSelectionModel.ts` / `setupSelectionModel.ts` are small, tested,\n   pure models (good). But playback-only prompts synthesized from log\n   patterns (`revealPromptForLogs`) duplicate what `RevealSessionLayer`\n   already animates — two systems now own \"show milled/revealed cards\",\n   violating the \"exactly one system animates an event\" invariant.\n\n## Recommended path\n\n**Unify live on the phase contract instead of patching the cumulative path.**\nThe local engine already receives per-decision observations (`autoSteps`);\nthose are natural phase boundaries. The shape:\n\n1. **Stable event identity at the source.** In `appendTimeline`, dedupe\n   incoming logs against a content-keyed cursor (the engine gives no log ids,\n   so key on the serialized log + a monotonic per-game sequence that tolerates\n   the per-player overlap). Duplicates get dropped, not re-id'd.\n2. **A live step builder** that turns each observation's *new* logs into a\n   step `{ events, view }` — the view being the board state *at that\n   observation*, seat-fixed to the viewer (always render from the human's\n   seat; opponent hand from `handCount`, own hand from the last own-perspective\n   observation — this replaces `withKnownHands` with an explicit rule instead\n   of a length heuristic). Synthesize serials the way the replay pipeline\n   does, so anchors regain precision.\n3. **Play steps through the same machinery replay uses** (the stepper in\n   `gameStore.apply` becomes the one consumer; `animateActions` stops being a\n   correctness switch and becomes pacing only). The gate keeps its replay\n   scope behavior; its live \"unseen tail\" mode shrinks to a no-op and can be\n   deleted.\n4. **Delete the compensations**: `withKnownHands`, `revealPromptForLogs` (the\n   reveal session layer already owns that animation), `isAgentDecisionView`\n   filtering (the step builder simply doesn't emit steps for agent decision\n   points).\n\nThis is a few focused days, mostly in `localEngine.ts`, reusing grouping\nlogic from `cabtReplay.ts` rather than duplicating it. It removes code on\nnet and makes live/replay share one honest contract, which is the\nsimplification you asked for.\n\n| Old piece | Verdict | Note |\n|---|---|---|\n| `AnimationEventGate` live mode | **Replace** | Phase steps make \"unseen tail\" unnecessary; keep replay scope logic |\n| `gameStore.apply` sequence loop (`game.svelte.ts:66`) | **Adapt** | Becomes the single step player for live phases; delays → pacing only |\n| `withKnownHands` (`localEngine.ts:457`) | **Replace** | Seat-fixed view builder with explicit own-hand rule |\n| `revealPromptForLogs` (`localEngine.ts:522`) | **Delete** | RevealSessionLayer owns reveal animation; prompt duplicated it |\n| `isAgentDecisionView` (`localEngine.ts:513`) | **Delete** | Step builder emits no step for agent decision points |\n| `promptSelectionModel` / `setupSelectionModel` | **Keep** | Pure, tested input models; restyle later if desired |\n| `cabtLogsToTimeline` (`logFormat.ts`) | **Adapt** | Add content-keyed identity + dedupe cursor |\n| Anchors / visibility / choreograph / layers | **Keep** | Feed them correct data; they already behave |\n\n## Quick fixes (status as of 2026-07-07 evening)\n\n1. **IMPLEMENTED — log dedupe.** `src/engine/logDedupe.ts` (content-signature\n   sliding window, 300 entries) filters every observation's logs in\n   `appendTimeline` before `cabtLogsToTimeline`; the deduper resets with the\n   session. Unit tests in `src/engine/logDedupe.test.ts`. Verified against a\n   live bridge session: 39 of 90 delivered logs were re-deliveries and all\n   were dropped, including the actor-switch observations behind symptom 1\n   (worst case raw=13 → kept=3).\n2. **IMPLEMENTED — turn-boundary claim release.** All three animation layers\n   take a `turnKey` prop (`turn-${game.turn}` in live, constant in replay)\n   and run `endScope()` / `clearSession()` when it changes, so no claim,\n   sprite, or reveal session outlives the turn that created it.\n3. **IMPLEMENTED — Step playback defaults ON** (`viewSettings.svelte.ts`), so\n   live events animate against each intermediate view instead of one burst\n   against the final board.\n4. **IMPLEMENTED — live reveal-session clearing** via the same `turnKey`\n   boundary in `RevealSessionLayer` (replay behavior unchanged; sessions that\n   continue into the incoming batch still survive the boundary).\n5. **IMPLEMENTED — animation-gated sequential playback** (follow-up to the\n   fixed-cadence problem: agent actions overlapped into garbled animations).\n   `src/lib/anim/activity.ts` is a shared busy-until signal: when a layer\n   schedules a live batch it reports the batch's scheduled end\n   (`scheduledEndMs` + handoff/settle padding), and `gameStore.apply` awaits\n   idle before applying the next sequence view (and before the first view of\n   a new response). \"Step ms\" is now the *minimum gap between views*, not the\n   cadence; per-step waits are capped at 5s so a stuck destination poll can't\n   deadlock playback. Playback-prompt confirms are unchanged. Replay pacing\n   untouched (it never consults the signal). Note this is interim mechanics:\n   the structural live-step builder below subsumes it — once live produces\n   proper phases with durations, the stepper can pace from phase metadata the\n   way replay does, and the busy-signal becomes a safety net only.\n\n### Still outstanding\n\n- **Dev overlay for stuck hides**: `animVisibility.hiddenCount()` already\n  exists; surface it in the debug settings panel to catch claim leaks early.\n- **Dedupe caveat** and **the \"Recommended path\" section above** —\n  **LANDED same day.** The seat-fixed live step builder shipped\n  (`src/engine/liveSteps.ts` + reworked `localEngine.appendSteps`), with\n  positional per-seat-stream dedupe instead of content dedupe (it pairs the\n  perspective-variant draws this caveat worried about — measured at roughly\n  one variant pair per draw, not \"occasional\"). `withKnownHands`,\n  `revealPromptForLogs`, `isAgentDecisionView`, `logDedupe`, and the gate's\n  live mode are deleted. Details and divergences:\n  `docs/audit-2026-07-07-viewer-play-pipeline.md`, \"Implementation\n  addendum\". {"parentUuid":"eb3f4c53-5bf9-4e47-afff-41c0858fa56f","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"38bde3ab-a47f-4b91-886b-2dfe1e9b27d1","agentId":"ab5a61a500485d254","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01S1bgUMdqY7vX7sekajFhNh","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# Audit: the live-play pipeline around the animations (2026-07-07)\n2\t\n3\tScope: the whole viewer play pipeline — App.svelte game flow → server.ts →\n4\tlocalEngine.ts → cabt_bridge.py → engine and back — plus seat/perspective\n5\thandling, format proliferation, the prompt system, this week's integration\n6\tseams, and the \"should the viewer consume cabt_service?\" question. This is the\n7\tlayer yesterday's audit (`audit-2026-07-07-live-play-animation.md`) did *not*\n8\tgo deep on. Baseline before any judgment: `npx vitest run` 225/225 green,\n9\t`tsc -p tsconfig.build.json --noEmit` clean. Claims marked \"probe\" were\n10\tverified against the real engine via a headless bridge session\n11\t(agent-vs-agent full game, official Abomasnow deck mirror).\n12\t\n13\t## Executive summary\n14\t\n15\tThe live-play layer is two codebases wearing one trenchcoat. Underneath is a\n16\tsmall, honest CABT core: a 232-line bridge speaking raw engine observations,\n17\tan option-index prompt path that already matches the engine's select model\n18\tend-to-end, and a pure observation→GameView projection. On top is the fossil\n19\tof a different engine — the ptcg-server-era interaction layer: a 20-class\n20\tprompt taxonomy of which live CABT emits **four**, a semantic command API\n21\t(`playCard`/`attack`-by-name/`useAbility`-by-name) that must be\n22\treverse-matched onto engine options by predicates, client-side legality\n23\tguessing that contradicts the engine, and roughly two thousand lines of\n24\tboard-prompt machinery (SetupDock, attach-energy assignment, damage\n25\tstrategies, target protocols) that is **unreachable in live play** — only the\n26\tprompt gallery can trigger it. The inconsistencies Charlie still sees are\n27\tmostly this layer fighting the engine's model: clicks that look legal but\n28\tbounce off the engine, Cancel buttons that can never succeed, retreat state\n29\tsmuggled across requests, and a seat model where \"active player\" means\n30\t\"whoever the engine is asking right now.\"\n31\t\n32\tTwo projections of the same data (live vs replay) have already drifted —\n33\tthey disagree on what a draw result is. And event identity, patched\n34\tyesterday with content-dedupe, is measurably still broken at the source:\n35\tin the probed game, 35 of 36 draws were delivered twice in different\n36\tper-seat encodings (both pass the filter), while six identical prize-set\n37\tlog lines inside one observation were collapsed to one (the filter\n38\tover-fires). Both directions are wrong; only the bridge can fix identity.\n39\t\n40\tThe from-scratch shape is one idea: **the engine's select is the only\n41\tinteraction contract.** Project every select (main phase included) as a\n42\tdecision with indexed options; every UI affordance derives from those\n43\toptions; one `select` command carries indexes back. That deletes the\n44\tmatchers, the legality guessing, the taxonomy, and most of App.svelte's\n45\twiring — and it composes cleanly with yesterday's seat-fixed step-builder\n46\tplan. Verdict on cabt_service: don't consume it (it's an LLM decision\n47\tboundary without per-step observations, in a private repo feeding a public\n48\tone); converge the agent contract and protocol shape instead.\n49\t\n50\t## The pipeline as-built\n51\t\n52\t```\n53\tApp.svelte (1,520 lines: mode/seat state, gesture wiring, prompt routing)\n54\t  └─ httpClient.ts  POST /local-engine {type, payload, sessionId}\n55\t       └─ vite proxy → server.ts (:8095, thin HTTP shim + agents/decks/save)\n56\t            └─ LocalEngineController (localEngine.ts, 975 lines)\n57\t                 ├─ command switch → option predicate matchers → applySelection\n58\t                 ├─ CabtBridgeClient (spawn, JSON-lines, no timeout)\n59\t                 │    └─ cabt_bridge.py (232 lines: battle_start/select,\n60\t                 │         in-process agent(obs) seats, auto-play loop)\n61\t                 ├─ withKnownHands / logDeduper / appendTimeline / replayFrames\n62\t                 └─ cabtObservationToGameView (demoEngine.ts) → GameView\n63\t                      └─ EngineResponse {view, sequence[], sessionId}\n64\t                           └─ gameStore.apply: animation-gated sequence playback\n65\t```\n66\t\n67\tReplay is a parallel universe: Kaggle/saved JSON → `cabtReplayToSnapshot`\n68\t(cabtReplay.ts, 2,806 lines) → its own `frameToGameView` → `replayStore`.\n69\tLive and replay meet only at the GameView type and the animation layers.\n70\t\n71\t## Findings, ranked by architectural weight\n72\t\n73\t### F1. The interaction layer is a fossil of another engine, and most of it is dead in live play\n74\t\n75\t**What.** The viewer's UI-facing contracts are inherited from a\n76\tptcg-server-style engine and were never re-derived for CABT:\n77\t\n78\t- A semantic command API — `playCard(playerIndex, handIndex, target)`,\n79\t  `attack(name)`, `useAbility(name, target)`, `concede`, … (`gameApi.ts:3-12`,\n80\t  `httpClient.ts:129-159`).\n81\t- A 20-class prompt taxonomy (`prompts.ts:3-23`) with a matching PromptHost\n82\t  dispatch (`PromptHost.svelte:46-79`).\n83\t- The `PlayerType`/`SlotType`/`CardTarget` addressing scheme and magic phase\n84\t  numbers 0/2/7 (`types.ts:1-21`, `demoEngine.ts:441`).\n85\t- Naming residue: `hostedAvailableActionsScope` (`httpClient.ts:55`).\n86\t\n87\tLive CABT emits exactly four prompt classes: `ChoosePrizePrompt`,\n88\t`ChooseCardsPrompt`, `SelectPrompt` (`demoEngine.ts:593,618,646`) and the\n89\tplayback-only `ConfirmCardsPrompt` (`localEngine.ts:539`). Everything else in\n90\tthe taxonomy is produced **only by prompt-gallery fixtures**\n91\t(`src/lib/prompt-gallery/fixtures.ts`); `cabtReplay.ts` emits zero prompts\n92\t(`cabtReplay.ts:2477`, `prompts: []`). Consequently all of the following can\n93\tnever trigger in a real game:\n94\t\n95\t- The setup board-placement flow: `SetupDock.svelte`, `setupSelection*`,\n96\t  `getSetupPromptUiState` — gated on `message === 'CHOOSE_STARTING_POKEMONS'`\n97\t  (`App.svelte:318`), a message no CABT path produces (live setup arrives as\n98\t  a `ChooseCardsPrompt` titled \"Choose Active Pokemon\",\n99\t  `demoEngine.ts:874`). Real setup is a card-list dialog; the nicer\n100\t  board-placement UX is dead weight.\n101\t- The three board strategies (`createPutDamageStrategy`,\n102\t  `createDamageTransferStrategy`, `createChoosePokemonStrategy`,\n103\t  `App.svelte:356-382`), `damageTransferStore`, the attach-energy assignment\n104\t  machinery in `promptSelectionStore`, and the whole\n105\t  `targets.ts` blocked/`playerType` field protocol (`targets.ts:54-91`).\n106\t- `AttachEnergyPrompt`, `EnergyTransferPrompt`, `CoinFlipPrompt`,\n107\t  `WaitPrompt`, `ChooseAttackPrompt`, `ShuffleOrderPrompt`, mulligan/alert\n108\t  hosts; the `ShuffleDeckPrompt` and `GO_FIRST` auto-resolve rules\n109\t  (`prompts.ts:85-95`).\n110\t- ~1,900 lines in these modules alone (excluding their tests), plus several\n111\t  hundred lines of `App.svelte` wiring (`App.svelte:241-350, 1015-1203`).\n112\t\n113\tAdjacent dead code in the same layer: `concede` is in the toolbar but always\n114\terrors (`localEngine.ts:137`); `listReplays`/`loadReplay`/`loadReplayData`\n115\tand the `/local-engine/replays*` endpoints are stubs with no callers\n116\t(`localEngine.ts:157-170`, `server.ts:65-90`); `hostedAvailableActionsScope`\n117\t/`hostedAvailableActionsOptions` and `localGameApi.state()` have zero call\n118\tsites (`httpClient.ts:55-77,114-116`); `commandApi` is a `$derived` of a\n119\tconstant (`App.svelte:130`); `CabtObservation.search_begin_input` is set only\n120\tby the demo controller and read by nothing (`types.ts:236`,\n121\t`demoEngine.ts:239`).\n122\t\n123\t**Why it matters.** This is the staleness the owner senses. Every live-play\n124\tchange threads through contracts that live play cannot exercise, App.svelte\n125\tcarries ~10 derived chains for prompts that never appear, and the prompt\n126\tgallery — not the game — is what keeps this code \"used.\" It also inverts the\n127\ttesting story: the best-tested interaction code is the unreachable half.\n128\t\n129\t### F2. The command surface duplicates the engine's select model — legality is guessed client-side, then re-derived server-side, and both guesses can be wrong\n130\t\n131\t**What.** The engine's `select.option` list is a complete, indexed statement\n132\tof what is legal right now. The viewer ignores it in the main phase and\n133\treconstructs it twice:\n134\t\n135\t1. **Client-side guessing.** Board affordances come from card metadata, not\n136\t   options: `canPlayCardToSlot` treats any name-matching evolution as\n137\t   playable (`playTargets.ts:50-52` — no `appearThisTurn`, no first-turn\n138\t   rule), any energy as attachable (`playTargets.ts:74-76` — no\n139\t   once-per-turn check), and `playableCardIds` is literally the whole hand\n140\t   (`demoEngine.ts:478`). `availableActions` (attacks/abilities/retreat) is\n141\t   option-derived and correct (`demoEngine.ts:735-773`) — so the same view\n142\t   mixes real legality with guessed legality.\n143\t2. **Server-side re-matching.** `playCard`/`attack`/`useAbility`/`retreat`/\n144\t   `passTurn` are translated back into an option index by predicates —\n145\t   `matchesPlayCardOption`, `matchesAttackOption` (attack **by name**,\n146\t   `localEngine.ts:576-581`), `matchesAbilityOption` (ability by first-skill\n147\t   name, `localEngine.ts:583-601,616-619`). A miss throws \"That action is not\n148\t   currently legal in the CABT engine\" (`localEngine.ts:270`).\n149\t\n150\tWhen the guess and the engine disagree, the user gets an error toast for a\n151\tclick the UI invited. Meanwhile the **prompt path already does it right**:\n152\tprompts carry option indexes end-to-end (`demoEngine.ts:599,624` →\n153\t`ChooseCardsPrompt.svelte:68` → `resolvePrompt` →\n154\t`normalizePromptSelection` → `applySelection`, `localEngine.ts:642-653`).\n155\tTwo interaction paradigms coexist in one controller; the lossy one owns the\n156\tmain phase.\n157\t\n158\tConcrete warts this produces today:\n159\t\n160\t- **Cancel buttons that cannot succeed.** Live prompt components offer\n161\t  Cancel resolving `null` (`SelectPrompt.svelte:102`,\n162\t  `ChooseCardsPrompt.svelte:133`, `ChoosePrizePrompt.svelte:102`); `null`\n163\t  normalizes to `[]` (`localEngine.ts:643-645`), and any select with\n164\t  `minCount >= 1` — i.e. nearly all of them — throws \"Selection must contain\n165\t  1-1 option(s)\" (`localEngine.ts:283-285`). Engine prompts are not\n166\t  cancellable; the affordance is a lie inherited from an engine where it\n167\t  wasn't.\n168\t- **Cross-request retreat state.** `pendingRetreatTarget`\n169\t  (`localEngine.ts:103,250-261,391-418`) smuggles the bench choice past\n170\t  intermediate energy-discard prompts by auto-consuming any later select\n171\t  that happens to contain a matching BENCH option for that seat. It is\n172\t  cleared only when consumed, on failure of the initial RETREAT match, or on\n173\t  session reset — there is no abandon path, so it survives arbitrary\n174\t  interleavings and can claim a later, unrelated bench choice.\n175\t- **The DISCARD_ENERGY batching special case.** The engine asks for energies\n176\t  one at a time; the UI wants one multi-select. The compensation spans both\n177\t  layers: `repeatedEnergyPaymentCount` fakes min/max in the projection\n178\t  (`demoEngine.ts:662-685`) and `applyRepeatedSingleSelections` replays\n179\t  single selects, re-finding each card by serial as options reshuffle\n180\t  (`localEngine.ts:310-357`). ~90 lines to hide one honest sequence of\n181\t  prompts.\n182\t\n183\t**Why it matters.** This layer is where \"issues and inconsistencies in live\n184\tplay\" are structurally guaranteed: two legality oracles that can disagree,\n185\tname-string action identity, hidden cross-request state, and error paths as\n186\tUX. None of it would exist if affordances were projections of options.\n187\t\n188\t### F3. The seat model conflates \"seat being asked\" with \"turn player\", and hand knowledge is a count-based heuristic\n189\t\n190\t**What.** Probe results against the real engine: `players[]` is seat-stable\n191\t(card `playerIndex` always equals array index), exactly the seat matching\n192\t`yourIndex` has a non-null hand, and `yourIndex` flips **mid-turn** whenever\n193\tthe engine needs the other seat's input — in one probed game, 4 of 9 flips\n194\twere mid-turn (setup placement, `DRAW_COUNT`, and two KO-replacement\n195\t`TO_ACTIVE` selects). The projection nevertheless defines\n196\t`activePlayerIndex = current.yourIndex` (`demoEngine.ts:436`) and everything\n197\tdownstream treats it as \"whose turn it is\": the status bar\n198\t(`App.svelte:1263`), board-follow rotation (`App.svelte:384-388`), action\n199\tgating (`canPlayerAct`, `playTargets.ts:87-89`), and `targetToCabt`'s\n200\tactor-relative addressing (`localEngine.ts:968-975`). The turn player is\n201\tactually derivable statelessly — `(firstPlayer + turn - 1) % 2` — but no\n202\tGameView field carries it, nor the viewer's own seat.\n203\t\n204\tThe same missing seat model forced `withKnownHands`\n205\t(`localEngine.ts:460-485`): hands vanish whenever the other seat is being\n206\tasked, so a cache re-attaches the last known hand — but only when\n207\t`handCount` matches the cached length. Equal-count changes (discard one,\n208\tdraw one) silently show stale cards; unequal counts degrade to serial-less\n209\tplaceholders (`demoEngine.ts:466-467`), which yesterday's audit traced into\n210\tanimation symptoms 2 and 3. Seat control is *also* duplicated: the server\n211\ttracks `playerControls` (`localEngine.ts:108,229`) while the client keeps its\n212\town copy in `activePlayerControls` (`App.svelte:105,503`) because GameView\n213\tsays nothing about seats; a reload desynchronizes them (module-level\n214\t`currentSessionId`, `httpClient.ts:27`, means the client can't reattach\n215\tanyway).\n216\t\n217\t**Why it matters.** Perspective is the suspected source of remaining\n218\tlive-play weirdness, and the model confirms it: the UI's one\n219\t\"active player\" concept is three distinct concepts (viewer seat, turn seat,\n220\tdeciding seat) that only coincide in the happy path. Every mid-turn forced\n221\tselect momentarily relabels the game as the opponent's.\n222\t\n223\t### F4. Event identity is still unsolved at the source — the dedupe filter both under- and over-fires (probe-verified)\n224\t\n225\t**What.** Yesterday's quick fix (content-keyed sliding window,\n226\t`logDedupe.ts`) treats log content as identity. The engine's delivery makes\n227\tthat wrong in both directions:\n228\t\n229\t- **Perspective-variant duplicates pass.** The engine re-delivers each seat's\n230\t  missed events in *that seat's* encoding: the drawing seat gets `Draw` with\n231\t  `cardId`, the other seat gets `DrawReverse` without. Probed game: 36 `Draw`\n232\t  vs 35 `DrawReverse` in one stream — essentially **every draw arrives\n233\t  twice**, in content the filter cannot pair. Both become timeline events\n234\t  (\"Player 2 drew Abomasnow.\" then \"Player 2 drew a card.\",\n235\t  `logFormat.ts:63-66`), so draws can double-animate — and the concrete\n236\t  variant **leaks hidden information**: agent-seat observations flow through\n237\t  `appendTimeline` regardless of seat (`localEngine.ts:487-518`), so the\n238\t  human-visible timeline (`LogPanel`) names the opponent's drawn cards.\n239\t  Yesterday's doc called this \"occasional\"; it is the common case.\n240\t- **Legitimate repeats are eaten.** Six identical prize-set lines\n241\t  (`{type:7, fromArea:1(DECK), toArea:6(PRIZE)}`, no serial) arrived inside\n242\t  one observation; the content-set keeps one (`logDedupe.ts:24-31` has no\n243\t  multiplicity), so five prize placements produce no event. Any repeated\n244\t  identical action within the 300-line window (same-result attack two turns\n245\t  running, multi-card reverse mills) is silently dropped.\n246\t- Total measured redundancy: 125 of 249 delivered lines were exact\n247\t  re-deliveries — the deduper is load-bearing, and it's the wrong tool.\n248\t\n249\t**Why it matters.** The animation backbone's core premise is stable event\n250\tidentity (yesterday's finding #1). Content-dedupe in the controller cannot\n251\tmanufacture identity that the transport destroyed. Only the bridge — which\n252\tsees every observation in order — can build a canonical event stream: keep\n253\tper-seat delivery cursors, emit each physical event once (preferring the\n254\tinformation-rich encoding for the *viewer's* seat and the reversed encoding\n255\tfor hidden info), and tag it with a monotonic sequence number.\n256\t\n257\t### F5. Format proliferation: two GameView projections, two observation typings, three option→card resolvers — already drifting\n258\t\n259\t**What.** Representations currently in play:\n260\t\n261\t1. Raw `CabtObservation` (`types.ts:232-237`) — bridge payload. Load-bearing.\n262\t2. `CabtVisualizeFrame` (`cabtReplay.ts:39-84`) — the same engine frame\n263\t   retyped independently for replay. Pure duplication.\n264\t3. `GameView` (`game/types.ts:147-160`) — the UI projection. Load-bearing.\n265\t4. Saved local replays: pseudo-Kaggle `{visualize, environment}`\n266\t   (`localEngine.ts:183-192`) — good convergence (one reader), but frames are\n267\t   saved *hydrated* with `withKnownHands` output, and they land in\n268\t   `public/game-logs/` which is not gitignored (runtime artifacts appear as\n269\t   untracked repo files; `public/local-replays` is ignored but unused).\n270\t5. Kaggle episode JSON (`cabtReplay.ts:86-106`) — external, must support.\n271\t6. `ReplaySnapshot`/`ReplayStep` (`game/replay.ts`) — replay pipeline output.\n272\t\n273\tThe duplications that hurt:\n274\t\n275\t- **Two projections.** `cabtObservationToGameView` (`demoEngine.ts:415-452`)\n276\t  vs `frameToGameView` (`cabtReplay.ts:2455-2481`) — parallel\n277\t  `buildPlayerView`s, parallel `stadiumForPlayer`s, and **divergent winner\n278\t  semantics**: replay maps engine result 2 → `winner: 3` → \"Draw\"\n279\t  (`cabtReplay.ts:2474`, `App.svelte:404-411`), live passes result through\n280\t  (`demoEngine.ts:445`) so a drawn live game reads \"Game finished\" and\n281\t  `saveReplay` records `result 2` (`localEngine.ts:202`).\n282\t- **Three option→card resolvers.** `cardForOption`+`attachedCardForOption`\n283\t  exist in localEngine (`localEngine.ts:367-389,955-966`) and demoEngine\n284\t  (`demoEngine.ts:810-861`) with different area coverage (demoEngine handles\n285\t  `cardId`/`deck`/`LOOKING`; localEngine's copy handles `LOOKING`/`STADIUM`\n286\t  but not `deck`), plus the replay pipeline's own frame-side lookups.\n287\t- **A third engine.** `CabtDemoController` (`demoEngine.ts:150-413`) is a\n288\t  931-line file whose top half is a hand-rolled mini-engine used only for\n289\t  `CABT_ENGINE_MODE=demo` and two scaffold tests — and it shares its module\n290\t  with the load-bearing projection, which is why the projection lives in a\n291\t  file named \"demoEngine\".\n292\t\n293\t**Why it matters.** Semantic decisions (winner mapping, hand visibility,\n294\tstadium ownership, option resolution) must be made once. Today each is made\n295\ttwo or three times, and the drift is no longer hypothetical.\n296\t\n297\t### F6. Bridge protocol robustness: unbounded waits and an unguarded stdout\n298\t\n299\t**What.** `CabtBridgeClient.request` registers a pending promise with **no\n300\ttimeout** (`localEngine.ts:698-704`); a wedged native engine or a lost\n301\tresponse hangs the HTTP request forever. And responses *can* be lost:\n302\tagents run in-process in the bridge, so `print()` writes to the protocol\n303\tstream. The viewer tolerates whole non-JSON lines (`localEngine.ts:761-768`,\n304\tcommit a126b72), but an agent printing **without a trailing newline** glues\n305\tits output to the next JSON response — the merged line fails parsing, is\n306\tdropped, and the pending request never resolves. The principled fix is in\n307\tthe bridge: point `sys.stdout` at stderr for the process and keep a private\n308\thandle to the real stdout for protocol writes (`cabt_bridge.py:228`).\n309\tSmaller: the parse-error path reuses a stale `message` id\n310\t(`cabt_bridge.py:227`), and macOS still defaults to Docker\n311\t(`localEngine.ts:786-820`) even though the engine now ships native\n312\tmac-arm64 builds — and Docker mode breaks workspace agents, whose manifest\n313\tpaths resolve to absolute host paths (`workspaceAgents.ts:66`) that don't\n314\texist inside the `/workspace` mount. Workspace agents effectively require\n315\t`CABT_ENGINE_MODE=native`; nothing says so.\n316\t\n317\t**Why it matters.** These are exactly the failure modes of \"agent seats +\n318\tsubprocess protocol\", i.e. the new integration surface. Every one is a\n319\tsilent hang or an environment-dependent break rather than an error message.\n320\t\n321\t### F7. Two repos, two agent contracts, two engine adapters\n322\t\n323\t**What.** The bridge and the harness have independently grown the same\n324\torgans: engine adaptation (`cabt_bridge.Session` vs `CabtEngineAdapter`,\n325\t`engine.py:44-121`), the auto-play-until-human loop (`cabt_bridge.py:135-150`\n326\tvs `session.py:203-224`), Kaggle agent loading (`load_agent`,\n327\t`cabt_bridge.py:47-85` vs `PythonFunctionPlayer`, `players.py:82-121`), and\n328\tdeck validation. Worse, they diverge on the deck-general agent contract: the\n329\tviewer **pushes** with a module-level `set_deck(deck, seat)` hook\n330\t(`cabt_bridge.py:47-50,106-108`) while the harness **pulls** with\n331\t`choose_deck(seat)` / a null-observation `agent()` call (`players.py:90-92`).\n332\tBoth semantics are legitimate (the viewer assigns decks; the harness lets\n333\tagents bring theirs), but an anyDeck agent like copycat needs a shim per\n334\trepo, and nothing documents which hook is canonical.\n335\t\n336\t**Why it matters.** The agent contract is the thing third parties (and your\n337\town farm) write against. Two dialects means every agent grows\n338\tcompatibility code, and drift compounds — see F6's stdout problem, which the\n339\tharness solves differently (out-of-process stdio service) than the viewer\n340\t(in-process + tolerant parser).\n341\t\n342\t## What fits well\n343\t\n344\tBeing fair — a lot of the CABT-native core is right:\n345\t\n346\t- **The bridge is the right kind of boundary.** 232 dependency-free lines,\n347\t  JSON-lines, raw observations, spawn-per-game neutralizing the engine's\n348\t  one-battle-per-process global state (`localEngine.ts:220`,\n349\t  `cabt_bridge.py:88-169`). Nothing here fights the engine.\n350\t- **The prompt path is the correct model, already shipped.** Option indexes\n351\t  flow untranslated from `select.option` to the click handler and back\n352\t  (`demoEngine.ts:599` → `ChooseCardsPrompt.svelte:68` →\n353\t  `localEngine.ts:642-653`). The from-scratch shape below is \"do this\n354\t  everywhere\", not something new.\n355\t- **Stale-prompt rejection server-side** before touching the bridge\n356\t  (`localEngine.ts:295-308`), with a test proving no bridge call\n357\t  (`localEngine.test.ts:434-486`).\n358\t- **The projection is a pure function** (`cabtObservationToGameView`) — no\n359\t  store coupling, trivially testable; the problem is its duplicate, not its\n360\t  design.\n361\t- **`workspaceAgents.ts` is a model integration seam**: 76 lines, pure\n362\t  manifest reading, tested, with the deck served through a clean endpoint\n363\t  (`server.ts:52-63`) and graceful absence (`catalog.ts:29-31`).\n364\t- **`saveReplay` converging on the Kaggle envelope** means one replay reader\n365\t  for three sources — the right instinct even before the cleanup F5 asks for.\n366\t- **`gameStore.apply`'s generation guards** around the async playback loop\n367\t  (`game.svelte.ts:41-122`) are careful and, as far as inspection and tests\n368\t  show, correct.\n369\t- **anyDeck's default-not-lock behavior** is implemented exactly as designed\n370\t  (`App.svelte:180-207`), with the locked/anyDeck distinction honored at\n371\t  start (`forcedDeckSource`, `App.svelte:565-567`).\n372\t\n373\t## The from-scratch shape\n374\t\n375\tDesign premise: the animation backbone (per-phase steps, semantic anchors)\n376\tand multi-agent play (0, 1, or 2 human seats) are first-class; the engine's\n377\tselect is the *only* interaction contract; every semantic decision is made\n378\tonce.\n379\t\n380\t**1. Selects all the way down.** GameView grows one field:\n381\t\n382\t```\n383\tdecision?: {\n384\t  seq: number;              // monotonic per game, assigned by the bridge\n385\t  seat: number;             // who the engine is asking\n386\t  kind: 'main' | 'choose-cards' | 'choose-option' | 'choose-prize' | ...\n387\t  min: number; max: number;\n388\t  options: Array<{ index; kind; card?; source?; target?; attackId?; label }>;\n389\t}\n390\t```\n391\t\n392\tprojected 1:1 from `select` (main phase included). Every affordance — hand\n393\tglow, attack button, retreat target, dialog row — derives from\n394\t`decision.options`; legality is presence. One command replaces eight:\n395\t`{type:'select', seq, indexes}`. The stale check becomes `seq` equality\n396\t(replacing the whole-state hash `promptIdForObservation`,\n397\t`demoEngine.ts:698-703`). Gesture→option mapping (click card, click bench\n398\tslot) moves client-side where the options already are, deleting the server\n399\tmatchers, `pendingRetreatTarget` (retreat becomes: select RETREAT, engine\n400\tprompts for bench, UI shows it — or auto-answers it from the drag target,\n401\tas *UI* policy), the Cancel lie, and the energy-batching pair (the UI can\n402\treplay single selects itself, or just show the honest sequence).\n403\t\n404\t**2. Seats as data.** GameView carries `viewerSeat`, `turnSeat`\n405\t(`(firstPlayer + turn - 1) % 2`), and `seats: [{control, name}]` from the\n406\tserver's `playerControls`. `activePlayerIndex` disappears in favor of\n407\t`decision.seat` where \"who is being asked\" is meant. The client's\n408\t`activePlayerControls` copy dies. Views are always projected from the\n409\tviewer's fixed seat: own hand from the last own-seat observation, opponent\n410\thand as count — an explicit rule replacing the `withKnownHands` length\n411\theuristic (this is yesterday's step-builder item 2; the seat model here is\n412\twhat makes it expressible).\n413\t\n414\t**3. Identity at the bridge.** The bridge tags each response observation\n415\twith `seq` and emits a canonical event stream: per-seat delivery cursors so\n416\teach physical event appears once, hidden-info encoding chosen by the\n417\tviewer's seat, stable synthesized serials. `logDedupe` and the timeline id\n418\tcounter die; the animation gate gets the stable identity it was designed\n419\tfor. (This subsumes yesterday's \"content-keyed cursor\" sketch — cursors in\n420\tthe bridge, not content hashing in the controller.)\n421\t\n422\t**4. One projection module.** A single `cabtProjection.ts` owning\n423\tobservation→GameView, option→card resolution, winner mapping, stadium\n424\townership — parameterized by hand-visibility policy (viewer-seat vs replay\n425\tomniscient). `cabtReplay.ts` keeps its grouping/phase pipeline but consumes\n426\tthe shared projector; `CabtVisualizeFrame` folds into `CabtObservation`.\n427\tThe demo controller is replaced by a recorded fixture (a saved real game\n428\tdrives the gallery and offline dev better than a hand-rolled mini-engine).\n429\t\n430\t**5. Prompt system.** `className` string dispatch shrinks to the CABT\n431\t`decision.kind` enum; PromptHost maps kinds to the four real components\n432\t(cards / options / prizes / reveal) plus the board-strip. The gallery keeps\n433\tits harness but its fixtures become captured real `select` payloads, so\n434\tgallery and game can no longer diverge. Board-driven setup placement — the\n435\tone genuinely desirable piece of the dead layer — gets rebuilt in miniature\n436\tagainst `SETUP_ACTIVE_POKEMON`/`SETUP_BENCH_POKEMON` decisions.\n437\t\n438\t### Keep / adapt / replace / delete\n439\t\n440\t| Piece | Verdict | Note |\n441\t|---|---|---|\n442\t| `cabt_bridge.py` | **Adapt** | stdout guard, seq numbers, per-seat cursors, canonical events |\n443\t| `CabtBridgeClient` | **Adapt** | add request timeout; otherwise keep |\n444\t| `server.ts` | **Keep** | drop dead `/replays*` endpoints |\n445\t| Command switch + matchers + `pendingRetreatTarget` + energy batcher (`localEngine.ts`) | **Replace** | single `select` command; gestures map client-side |\n446\t| `cabtObservationToGameView` (demoEngine.ts) | **Adapt** | becomes the one projector, new module |\n447\t| `CabtDemoController` + demo data | **Delete** | recorded-game fixture replaces `CABT_ENGINE_MODE=demo` |\n448\t| `frameToGameView` + frame types (cabtReplay.ts) | **Replace** | consume shared projector; keep grouping/phases |\n449\t| `prompts.ts` taxonomy, PromptHost dispatch | **Replace** | `decision.kind` enum |\n450\t| `playTargets.ts` legality guessing | **Replace** | derive from `decision.options` |\n451\t| SetupDock, `setupSelection*`, attach machinery, `damageTransfer*`, `strategies/`, `targets.ts` | **Delete** | live-unreachable; rebuild setup placement small, from decisions |\n452\t| `gameApi.ts`, `hostedAvailableActions*`, `concede`, `state()` | **Delete** | dead or always-error |\n453\t| `withKnownHands`, `revealPromptForLogs`, `isAgentDecisionView`, `logDedupe` | **Delete** | per yesterday's plan, enabled by 2+3 |\n454\t| `httpClient.ts` | **Adapt** | one `select` sender + start/save |\n455\t| `saveReplay` + Kaggle envelope | **Keep** | write raw (unhydrated) frames; move output under a gitignored dir |\n456\t| `workspaceAgents.ts`, agents/decks endpoints, anyDeck flow | **Keep** | align deck hook with harness (F7) |\n457\t| `gameStore.apply` playback, animation layers | **Keep** | consume steps per yesterday's table |\n458\t\n459\t### Migration order\n460\t\n461\tEach step lands green on its own. Status (2026-07-07):\n462\t\n463\t1. **Bridge hygiene** (F6) — **DONE** (`fb3813f`): protocol fd owned by the\n464\t   bridge (agent prints can't corrupt it), request timeout\n465\t   (CABT_BRIDGE_TIMEOUT_MS), stale-id fix. Sequence numbers landed as\n466\t   controller-side `decisionSeq` (step 3) plus the normalizer's positional\n467\t   cursors (step 4) — no protocol change was needed.\n468\t2. **One projector** (F5) — **DONE** (`267b311`): `cabtProjection.ts` owns\n469\t   observation→GameView for live and replay; winner/draw and stadium\n470\t   drift fixed; third option→card resolver deleted.\n471\t3. **Decisions** (F2/F1) — **DONE**: `GameView.decision` projected 1:1 from\n472\t   every select (main phase included), `GameView.seats`/`turnSeat` as data,\n473\t   one `select {seq, indexes}` command; the eight semantic commands,\n474\t   matchers, client legality guessing, `pendingRetreatTarget`, the\n475\t   DISCARD_ENERGY batching, Cancel-on-mandatory, the demo mini-engine, and\n476\t   the client-side seat-control copy are gone. Board-target decisions (new\n477\t   active after KO, switch/retreat destinations) are now answered by\n478\t   clicking the highlighted slot. Gallery fixtures are captured from real\n479\t   engine selects (`scripts/capture-decision-fixtures.ts`).\n480\t4. **Seat model + step builder** (F3/F4) — **DONE** (`5b8d458`,\n481\t   landed ahead of order): seat-fixed live steps with positional\n482\t   per-seat-stream identity; withKnownHands/revealPromptForLogs/\n483\t   isAgentDecisionView/logDedupe/gate-live-mode deleted.\n484\t5. **The sweep** (F1/F5) — **DONE** (`37834f6`, following the select\n485\t   contract in `7b272c9`): the ptcg-era prompt taxonomy and components,\n486\t   setup/attach/damage stores and strategies, targets/playTargets/preview,\n487\t   promptLifecycle, dead /replays endpoints, autoConfirmPrompts, and\n488\t   `GameView.prompts`/`PromptView` themselves are deleted outright — git\n489\t   history is the archive (`git show 37834f6` lists everything removed;\n490\t   the demo mini-engine went in `7b272c9`). The prompt gallery survives on\n491\t   decisions captured from real engine games.\n492\t\n493\tAll five steps are implemented. The remaining recommendations of this\n494\taudit that are intentionally NOT code changes: the cabt_service verdict\n495\t(converge contracts, don't consume) and the harness-side `set_deck`\n496\tsupport (F7) live in the other repo.\n497\t\n498\t## Should the viewer consume cabt_service instead?\n499\t\n500\t**No — keep the in-repo bridge; converge the contracts.**\n501\t\n502\tWhat consuming it would buy: one engine adapter, one agent loader, one\n503\tauto-play loop (~150 duplicated lines today), seeds, decision recording,\n504\tand a protocol already designed for external drivers\n505\t(`cabt_service/protocol.py:38-50`).\n506\t\n507\tWhy it loses:\n508\t\n509\t- **It's a decision boundary, not a visualization feed.** `choose_action`\n510\t  returns opponent auto-play as `{player, source, labels}` summaries\n511\t  (`session.py:296-300`) — no per-step observations. The viewer's animation\n512\t  pipeline lives on exactly those intermediate observations (`autoSteps`).\n513\t  Feeding the viewer would require a protocol extension (per-step\n514\t  `after_observation` streaming), i.e. redesigning the service into what\n515\t  the bridge already is.\n516\t- **The repo boundary points the wrong way.** The harness is private; the\n517\t  viewer is public. Today a public clone plus the Kaggle bundle gives\n518\t  working live play. A dependency on private code breaks that, and the\n519\t  service can't be vendored into the public repo.\n520\t- **The duplication is small and cold.** The overlapping code is ~150\n521\t  stable lines that change when the engine changes (rarely), not when the\n522\t  viewer changes (weekly).\n523\t\n524\tWhat *should* converge:\n525\t\n526\t- **The agent contract (F7).** Pick one deck-hook story — support\n527\t  `set_deck(deck, seat)` in the harness's `PythonFunctionPlayer` (push) and\n528\t  keep `choose_deck` as the pull for self-decked agents — and document it in\n529\t  one place both repos cite.\n530\t- **Protocol shape.** Adopt the service's envelope (`{id, ok, result|error}`)\n531\t  and error style in the bridge so tooling and mental models transfer; the\n532\t  bridge effectively becomes \"cabt_service's little sibling with an\n533\t  observation stream\", by design rather than accident.\n534\t- **Revisit only if** the harness becomes public/pip-installable *and* grows\n535\t  an observation-streaming mode; then the bridge could shrink to a launcher.\n536\t\n537\t## Test coverage of the play path\n538\t\n539\tBaseline: 225 tests green, tsc clean. Distribution is inverted relative to\n540\trisk:\n541\t\n542\t- **Strong**: replay pipeline (`cabtReplay.test.ts`, plus animation tests —\n543\t  ~3.8k lines), pure input models (`promptSelectionModel`,\n544\t  `setupSelectionModel` — much of which guards live-dead code, see F1),\n545\t  `logDedupe`, `workspaceAgents`, deck import, episodes parsing.\n546\t- **Thin where it hurts**: `localEngine.test.ts` tests private internals via\n547\t  `as any` with hand-built option shapes (`localEngine.test.ts:96-174`) and\n548\t  mocked bridges — it *encodes* the matchers' assumptions about engine\n549\t  payloads rather than verifying them. Nothing anywhere runs\n550\t  `cabt_bridge.py`; nothing plays a game through the real engine; nothing\n551\t  covers `withKnownHands`, `server.ts`, or the App.svelte flow (zero\n552\t  component tests). Every live-play regression this week was found by\n553\t  playing.\n554\t- **Cheapest high-value addition**: one env-gated integration test\n555\t  (`CABT_SAMPLE_SUBMISSION_DIR` present → spawn the real bridge, play an\n556\t  agent-vs-agent game — the probe for this audit did so in ~2s) asserting\n557\t  the invariants this audit leaned on: seat-stable `players[]`, hand\n558\t  visibility ≡ `yourIndex`, monotonic decision flow, result mapping, and —\n559\t  once F4 lands — no duplicate canonical events. Second: a golden-file test\n560\t  replaying a recorded bridge session through `LocalEngineController` and\n561\t  snapshotting `view`/`sequence`, so controller changes diff visibly.\n562\t\n563\t## Implementation addendum (landed same day)\n564\t\n565\tMigration step 4's live half — the seat-fixed step builder — was implemented\n566\timmediately after this audit (the commit following the audit commit),\n567\trefined by the findings above. What landed:\n568\t\n569\t- **`src/engine/liveSteps.ts` — `LiveObservationNormalizer`.** Per-seat\n570\t  stream cursors give every delivered log line a global event index;\n571\t  re-deliveries are dropped *positionally*, not by content. This diverges\n572\t  deliberately from both yesterday's sketch (\"content-keyed cursor\") and the\n573\t  original quick fix: position pairs the `Draw`/`DrawReverse` perspective\n574\t  variants that content matching cannot (F4's under-dedupe) and keeps\n575\t  legitimately identical repeated lines (F4's over-dedupe). It also\n576\t  corrects this audit's own claim that \"only the bridge can build a\n577\t  canonical event stream\": the controller receives the same complete\n578\t  per-seat streams, so the cursor works one layer up with no protocol\n579\t  change. Validated live: 544 re-delivered lines across a real game, zero\n580\t  positional mismatches (`liveBridge.integration.test.ts`).\n581\t- **Event-sourced hands with synthesized identity for the unknowable.**\n582\t  (Upgraded same day after Charlie's QA.) The non-acting seat's hand is\n583\t  exact event-driven state: the last hand-visible observation is the base,\n584\t  and the canonical stream's hand-mutating events apply on top (DRAW /\n585\t  MOVE_CARD-to-hand append the concrete card; PLAY/ATTACH/EVOLVE\n586\t  announcements and MOVE_CARD-from-hand remove by exact serial; reversed\n587\t  encodings append or take placeholders with stable negative serials). The\n588\t  mapping was validated against real games — zero drift at every\n589\t  own-observation checkpoint across three matchups — and the observation's\n590\t  `handCount` remains a safety net, not the mechanism. Cards whose\n591\t  identity the stream genuinely hasn't delivered yet (e.g. a face-down\n592\t  prize taken just before the turn passed) render as backs until the\n593\t  seat's own observation names them. Playback step views also carry\n594\t  `seats`, so the viewer's own hand is never treated as concealed during\n595\t  opponent-turn playback. One factual correction to yesterday's audit:\n596\t  live observations *do* carry serials on every known card (hand, board,\n597\t  discard — probe-verified); only hidden cards ever needed synthesis.\n598\t- **Hidden-info visibility policy** (from F4): a concealed seat's `DRAW`\n599\t  events are downgraded to the opponent-facing `DRAW_REVERSE` encoding, so\n600\t  a human no longer sees the agent's drawn cards in the timeline or as\n601\t  face-up draw animations. Agent-vs-agent games stay omniscient\n602\t  (spectator). Residual: rarer concrete `MOVE_CARD` encodings (deck\n603\t  searches) still pass through first-delivery; per-event encoding selection\n604\t  remains bridge work.\n605\t- **Live playback steps are replay-shaped.** `localEngine.appendSteps`\n606\t  emits one step per event-bearing observation — exactly its own events\n607\t  against the board state at that observation, prompts stripped (history\n608\t  frames never prompt, which subsumes the old agent-decision filtering).\n609\t  The interactive view keeps the cumulative timeline for the log panel;\n610\t  `App.svelte` feeds the animation layers only during playback, so the\n611\t  cumulative list never re-enters the gate.\n612\t- **The gate lost its live mode.** `AnimationEventGate` is now one rule:\n613\t  scope change animates the step's whole event list, unchanged scope\n614\t  animates nothing (`gate.ts`); `actionAnimationBatchEvents` and its\n615\t  unseen-id tracking are gone. `turnKey` stays: reveal sessions\n616\t  legitimately span multiple live steps within a turn, and the turn\n617\t  boundary remains their (and stuck claims') backstop.\n618\t- **Deleted:** `withKnownHands`/`knownHands`, `revealPromptForLogs` and the\n619\t  entire playback-prompt pause machinery (`gameStore`\n620\t  `waitForPlaybackConfirm`/`confirmPlaybackPrompt`, `App.svelte` and\n621\t  `prompts.ts` `playbackOnly` branches), `isAgentDecisionView`,\n622\t  `logDedupe.ts`. One semantic change: `animateActions` off now means no\n623\t  action animations at all (previously it burst-animated the cumulative\n624\t  tail against the final board — the failure mode quick fix #3 existed to\n625\t  avoid).\n626\t- **Tests:** unit coverage for the normalizer (positional dedupe, seat\n627\t  fixing, visibility) and the step builder; plus the env-gated real-engine\n628\t  integration suite this audit recommended\n629\t  (`liveBridge.integration.test.ts`: normalizer vs independent positional\n630\t  ground truth over a live game, full agent-vs-agent controller game with\n631\t  step-coherence assertions, concealment check). Run with\n632\t  `CABT_SAMPLE_SUBMISSION_DIR=… PYTHON=… npx vitest run liveBridge`;\n633\t  `CABT_PROBE_AGENT` optionally seats a real agent file.\n634\t\n635\t## Polish backlog (recorded, not built)\n636\t\n637\t- **Click-the-revealed-cards prompts** (Charlie, 2026-07-07): selection\n638\t  prompts for revealed cards should let the player click the reveal-layer\n639\t  sprites directly instead of a separate dialog — the sprites would carry\n640\t  decision option indexes as click targets. The select contract makes this\n641\t  clean; the reveal layer already knows each sprite's serial, and decisions\n642\t  resolve card→option via `cardForOption`.\n643\t- **Select-shape inventory + coverage guard** (planned follow-up to the\n644\t  effect-selector; same pattern as animation coverage): enumerate the\n645\t  structural signatures the engine's selects can take (option kinds ×\n646\t  min/max × countdown fields × target areas), rate each signature's UI\n647\t  affordance (board-click / card grid / labeled list), and add a guard test\n648\t  that surfaces any newly observed signature that only gets the plain\n649\t  fallback. `effectSelector.ts` + `boardDecisionOptions` are the first\n650\t  recognized signatures; the universal `SelectPrompt` fallback is the\n651\t  safety floor the guard measures against.\n652\t- **Full-deck search dialog** (Charlie, 2026-07-08; inventory-confirmed):\n653\t  from_deck selects deliver `select.deck` = the entire remaining deck while\n654\t  `select.option` lists only the legal picks. Real-PTCG presentation: show\n655\t  the whole deck in the search dialog, legal targets selectable, the rest\n656\t  visible but inert.
