{"parentUuid":"dd20e504-8fac-485c-a1b8-a3e6515468cc","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"4efcb21a-f499-4ac1-955b-398653e0632c","agentId":"ab5a61a500485d254","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01V6qiWstuPX86Q8RDLJJwFx","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# Component Animation Notes\n2\t\n3\t- Keep board and pile animations in the same transformed frame as the board. Prefer destination-owned animations, such as a pseudo-element or child anchored to the final slot, so the card does not snap when the animation hands off to the real UI.\n4\t- For animations that cross from flat UI into the tilted board, a fixed animation layer is acceptable only when it maps the card to the exact final viewport quad. Do not use approximate fixed overlays for board destinations.\n5\t- When replay state already contains the destination card, hide that real destination content until the animated card arrives. This avoids showing the animated card and final card at the same time.\n6\t- Drive animations from structured event fields, serials, and stable `data-*` anchors instead of parsing log text.\n7\t\n8\t## Replay Animation Invariants\n9\t\n10\t- Replay animations must be replayable. If a user scrubs away from a step and returns, the same phase should animate again. Use per-scope de-duping only to suppress duplicate work during the current render/phase, and clear it when the replay scope changes.\n11\t- Prefer phase-scoped action timelines for phase-owned animations. A replay step can contain several logical phases, and using the whole step timeline from a component that should animate one phase can cause skipped source states or duplicate animation.\n12\t- Guard replay phase timers against stale callbacks. A timer created for one step/phase must not advance a later step after the user scrubs.\n13\t\n14\t## Board-Origin Cards\n15\t\n16\t- Cards that start on the board and end on the board should stay in the board plane for the whole animation. Avoid viewport/fixed layers unless the animation explicitly transitions between UI coordinate systems.\n17\t- Cards that end on the board should also finish in the board plane. Deck-to-bench and deck-to-active effects, such as Buddy-Buddy Poffin, should use board-local motion layers rather than fixed reveal overlays; otherwise the card appears to leave the tilted table and snap back into perspective at handoff.\n18\t- If an attached card is represented as a small badge or crop on the board, do not animate a full card from the badge rectangle. Use the owning Pokemon card footprint when the intended effect is a full card sliding out from under that Pokemon.\n19\t- Preserve visual stacking intent: source Pokemon should be able to occlude a card that slides out from underneath it, but destination piles should not occlude cards that are landing on top of them.\n20\t- Target the visible destination surface, not the broad container. For discard piles, land on the `.discard-card-top .card-tile` when it exists; landing on the pile button/container often looks like the card goes to the bottom and then flickers to the top.\n21\t- Handoff should be identity-specific. Hide only the real destination card for the serial/card being animated, and keep the animated sprite alive long enough for the final DOM card to appear without a one-frame flash.\n22\t- Do not fade out a moving card before the destination card is painted underneath it. The usual handoff should be: keep the sprite fully visible through its final frame, reveal the destination DOM in the same position, then remove the sprite after a short settle window.\n23\t- For batched placement animations with staggered starts, such as two Poffin targets, do not let the first sprite hand off before the whole placement phase is ready. Earlier sprites may need to hold at their final position until the last staggered card and phase transition have caught up.\n24\t\n25\t## Resolving Trainer Effects\n26\t\n27\t- A played Trainer that has follow-up phases should stay in the play zone until every effect phase has resolved. Do not let it appear in discard during intermediate deck search, bench placement, attach, switch, draw, shuffle, or damage phases.\n28\t- Cards like Buddy-Buddy Poffin should read as one resolving effect: the Trainer is played, deck cards move to the board, the deck shuffles if needed, and only then does the Trainer move to discard. The Trainer should not flicker between play zone and discard while the benched Pokemon land.\n29\t- Search/reveal effects should make the chosen card visually clear. Keep selected cards distinct and stable while unselected revealed cards return or shuffle back, instead of splitting reveal and selection into unrelated-looking replay steps.\n30\t- When a selected reveal card later moves to hand, normalize from the selected card's current visual center at the start of the take phase. Avoid timer-based geometry rewrites at the end of the reveal phase; they create the small growth/shrink stutters that look like flicker.\n31\t"}]},"uuid":"2797a91a-f645-444b-8c56-229a8235a1f7","timestamp":"2026-07-09T03:12:52.879Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/Users/charlielockyer/Documents/Code/ai-battle-challenge/cabt-viewer/src/lib/components/AGENTS.md","content":"# Component Animation Notes\n\n- Keep board and pile animations in the same transformed frame as the board. Prefer destination-owned animations, such as a pseudo-element or child anchored to the final slot, so the card does not snap when the animation hands off to the real UI.\n- For animations that cross from flat UI into the tilted board, a fixed animation layer is acceptable only when it maps the card to the exact final viewport quad. Do not use approximate fixed overlays for board destinations.\n- When replay state already contains the destination card, hide that real destination content until the animated card arrives. This avoids showing the animated card and final card at the same time.\n- Drive animations from structured event fields, serials, and stable `data-*` anchors instead of parsing log text.\n\n## Replay Animation Invariants\n\n- Replay animations must be replayable. If a user scrubs away from a step and returns, the same phase should animate again. Use per-scope de-duping only to suppress duplicate work during the current render/phase, and clear it when the replay scope changes.\n- Prefer phase-scoped action timelines for phase-owned animations. A replay step can contain several logical phases, and using the whole step timeline from a component that should animate one phase can cause skipped source states or duplicate animation.\n- Guard replay phase timers against stale callbacks. A timer created for one step/phase must not advance a later step after the user scrubs.\n\n## Board-Origin Cards\n\n- Cards that start on the board and end on the board should stay in the board plane for the whole animation. Avoid viewport/fixed layers unless the animation explicitly transitions between UI coordinate systems.\n- Cards that end on the board should also finish in the board plane. Deck-to-bench and deck-to-active effects, such as Buddy-Buddy Poffin, should use board-local motion layers rather than fixed reveal overlays; otherwise the card appears to leave the tilted table and snap back into perspective at handoff.\n- If an attached card is represented as a small badge or crop on the board, do not animate a full card from the badge rectangle. Use the owning Pokemon card footprint when the intended effect is a full card sliding out from under that Pokemon.\n- Preserve visual stacking intent: source Pokemon should be able to occlude a card that slides out from underneath it, but destination piles should not occlude cards that are landing on top of them.\n- Target the visible destination surface, not the broad container. For discard piles, land on the `.discard-card-top .card-tile` when it exists; landing on the pile button/container often looks like the card goes to the bottom and then flickers to the top.\n- Handoff should be identity-specific. Hide only the real destination card for the serial/card being animated, and keep the animated sprite alive long enough for the final DOM card to appear without a one-frame flash.\n- Do not fade out a moving card before the destination card is painted underneath it. The usual handoff should be: keep the sprite fully visible through its final frame, reveal the destination DOM in the same position, then remove the sprite after a short settle window.\n- For batched placement animations with staggered starts, such as two Poffin targets, do not let the first sprite hand off before the whole placement phase is ready. Earlier sprites may need to hold at their final position until the last staggered card and phase transition have caught up.\n\n## Resolving Trainer Effects\n\n- A played Trainer that has follow-up phases should stay in the play zone until every effect phase has resolved. Do not let it appear in discard during intermediate deck search, bench placement, attach, switch, draw, shuffle, or damage phases.\n- Cards like Buddy-Buddy Poffin should read as one resolving effect: the Trainer is played, deck cards move to the board, the deck shuffles if needed, and only then does the Trainer move to discard. The Trainer should not flicker between play zone and discard while the benched Pokemon land.\n- Search/reveal effects should make the chosen card visually clear. Keep selected cards distinct and stable while unselected revealed cards return or shuffle back, instead of splitting reveal and selection into unrelated-looking replay steps.\n- When a selected reveal card later moves to hand, normalize from the selected card's current visual center at the start of the take phase. Avoid timer-based geometry rewrites at the end of the reveal phase; they create the small growth/shrink stutters that look like flicker.\n","numLines":31,"startLine":1,"totalLines":31}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"dd20e504-8fac-485c-a1b8-a3e6515468cc","sessionKind":"bg","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/charlielockyer/Documents/Code/ai-battle-challenge","sessionId":"6a7c23ff-6d4a-455f-bf85-fa444b0d588f","version":"2.1.205","gitBranch":"main"}

{"parentUuid":"1b5d6f3e-07dd-4902-8a5c-b7774eb6e3a2","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"4efcb21a-f499-4ac1-955b-398653e0632c","agentId":"ab5a61a500485d254","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01QFNKTbPDUUyAjqT94S7DKs","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# CABT Viewer Agent Notes\n2\t\n3\t# Project Shape\n4\t\n5\tThis is the Svelte 5 viewer for CABT battle states and replays. The\n6\tgoal is not to make a generic app shell or a demo UI. The goal is a readable,\n7\tfast, faithful play surface where the board state is obvious and the player can\n8\tact without fighting the interface.\n9\t\n10\t## Keep It Simple\n11\t\n12\tKISS: keep it simple. We do not like hacks. We like clean, robust code that\n13\tfollows normal frontend and Svelte best practices. Dumb hacks, brittle special\n14\tcases, and clever fixes that only work for one screenshot are not acceptable.\n15\t\n16\t## Build For Obviousness\n17\t\n18\tFight for obvious UI. If a card is playable, selected, attached, damaged,\n19\thovered, or being targeted by a prompt, that state should be visually clear\n20\twithout explanation. Prefer direct visual mappings over clever abstractions:\n21\tcards should look like cards, attachments should sit on the Pokemon they belong\n22\tto, and scroll/overflow affordances should appear where the player needs them.\n23\t\n24\tWhen a visual detail feels wrong, fix the underlying layout or component rule\n25\tinstead of piling on z-index tricks, magic offsets, or wrappers that only happen\n26\tto work for the current screenshot. Shadows, hover states, selected states,\n27\tmasks, and overlays should have enough layout room to render cleanly.\n28\t\n29\tDo not shrink important cards just to make overflow easier. Preserve card scale\n30\tand board readability unless the user explicitly asks for smaller cards. Prefer\n31\tscrolling, stable responsive tokens, and clear layout constraints.\n32\t\n33\t## Svelte 5\n34\t\n35\tUse Svelte 5 patterns. Prefer `$state`, `$derived`, and `$effect` for component\n36\tstate and reactivity. Keep state local when it belongs to one component. Do not\n37\tintroduce stores, context, or global coordination for one-off UI behavior.\n38\t\n39\tUse the existing component primitives and tokens before adding new structure:\n40\t`CardTile`, `BoardSlot`, `Hand`, `SelectableCard`, `PromptPanel`, and the sizing\n41\ttokens in `TableShell.svelte` and `styles/tokens.css`.\n42\t\n43\t## Rewrite Freely\n44\t\n45\tWe are not optimizing for extreme legacy compatibility inside this app. If a\n46\tfirst version of a feature needs to change a few prompts later, do not layer\n47\tcompatibility slop on top of it. Remove or replace the earlier approach when\n48\tthat produces simpler, clearer code.\n49\t\n50\tIt is fine to throw out code that no longer matches the product direction. Smart\n51\tagents can write better code than they can maintain a pile of special cases.\n52\tPrefer one clean current path over preserving several historical paths.\n53\t\n54\t## Visual QA\n55\t\n56\tFor UI changes, reason through the actual states the player will see: active\n57\tPokemon, benched Pokemon, hand cards, overflowing hands, prompt dialogs, hover,\n58\tselected, disabled, face-down, and attached-card states.\n59\t\n60\tWatch especially for clipping, accidental shrinking, layout shifts, text\n61\toverlap, mismatched scale between active and bench views, and shadows or glows\n62\tbeing cut off by scroll containers.\n63\t\n64\t## Animation Development\n65\t\n66\tRead `docs/replay-animation-architecture.md` before touching animation code.\n67\tThe short version: `choreograph()` in `src/lib/anim/motions.ts` is the single\n68\tclassifier from timeline events to motions and target effects; the render\n69\tlayers (`BoardAnimationLayer`, `ViewportAnimationLayer`, `RevealSessionLayer`)\n70\tresolve anchors and execute; all animation-time hiding goes through\n71\t`animVisibility` and the one `data-anim-hidden` attribute.\n72\t\n73\tRules that keep this system flicker-free:\n74\t\n75\t- One system animates a given event. New animation behavior goes into the\n76\t  choreographer and an existing layer; do not add per-component event\n77\t  classification, private hidden attributes, or component-local hide maps.\n78\t- Sprites render from view data through `BoardSlot`/`CardTile`. Never clone\n79\t  live DOM for a sprite, and never let an anchor query resolve inside a\n80\t  `[data-anim-layer]` subtree.\n81\t- When the final game state already contains the destination card, hide that\n82\t  destination with a visibility claim only until handoff. When the final state\n83\t  omits the source, use the pre-render snapshots (hand cards, attached badges)\n84\t  rather than letting the source pop out early.\n85\t- Timers belong to a layer, guarded by its generation counter, and are cleared\n86\t  on scope changes and destroy. In replay, board-space sprites and claims hold\n87\t  until the phase scope ends; the phase transition is the handoff. Do not\n88\t  reveal old slots from inside a renderer.\n89\t- Board-plane and viewport animations are different coordinate spaces. A card\n90\t  that starts and ends on the tilted board stays inside the board plane\n91\t  (offset-sum geometry); a card crossing between hand and board uses the\n92\t  viewport layer and the homography in `planeGeometry.ts`.\n93\t- Preserve the animation look. Keyframes, easings, and timing constants are\n94\t  the product; change them deliberately, not as a refactor side effect.\n95\t\n96\t## Checks\n97\t\n98\tDo not run expensive checks reflexively after every small CSS tweak. Agents are\n99\texpected to reason carefully.\n100\t\n101\tRun `npm run build` and `npm test` for larger changes, behavior changes, shared\n102\tcomponent changes, prompt-selection logic, game-state logic, or before committing\n103\ta meaningful batch. For very small visual-only edits, a targeted inspection is\n104\toften enough.\n105\t\n106\t## Public Boundary\n107\t\n108\tDo not add Kaggle native binaries, raw competition bundles, or generated local\n109\tmatch artifacts to this repo. Local CABT play should consume user-supplied\n110\tresources through `CABT_SAMPLE_SUBMISSION_DIR`.\n111\t"}]},"uuid":"6fc9e833-8aea-4b33-9463-fbc673efd625","timestamp":"2026-07-09T03:12:52.981Z","toolUseResult":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/Users/charlielockyer/Documents/Code/ai-battle-challenge/cabt-viewer/AGENTS.md","content":"# CABT Viewer Agent Notes\n\n# Project Shape\n\nThis is the Svelte 5 viewer for CABT battle states and replays. The\ngoal is not to make a generic app shell or a demo UI. The goal is a readable,\nfast, faithful play surface where the board state is obvious and the player can\nact without fighting the interface.\n\n## Keep It Simple\n\nKISS: keep it simple. We do not like hacks. We like clean, robust code that\nfollows normal frontend and Svelte best practices. Dumb hacks, brittle special\ncases, and clever fixes that only work for one screenshot are not acceptable.\n\n## Build For Obviousness\n\nFight for obvious UI. If a card is playable, selected, attached, damaged,\nhovered, or being targeted by a prompt, that state should be visually clear\nwithout explanation. Prefer direct visual mappings over clever abstractions:\ncards should look like cards, attachments should sit on the Pokemon they belong\nto, and scroll/overflow affordances should appear where the player needs them.\n\nWhen a visual detail feels wrong, fix the underlying layout or component rule\ninstead of piling on z-index tricks, magic offsets, or wrappers that only happen\nto work for the current screenshot. Shadows, hover states, selected states,\nmasks, and overlays should have enough layout room to render cleanly.\n\nDo not shrink important cards just to make overflow easier. Preserve card scale\nand board readability unless the user explicitly asks for smaller cards. Prefer\nscrolling, stable responsive tokens, and clear layout constraints.\n\n## Svelte 5\n\nUse Svelte 5 patterns. Prefer `$state`, `$derived`, and `$effect` for component\nstate and reactivity. Keep state local when it belongs to one component. Do not\nintroduce stores, context, or global coordination for one-off UI behavior.\n\nUse the existing component primitives and tokens before adding new structure:\n`CardTile`, `BoardSlot`, `Hand`, `SelectableCard`, `PromptPanel`, and the sizing\ntokens in `TableShell.svelte` and `styles/tokens.css`.\n\n## Rewrite Freely\n\nWe are not optimizing for extreme legacy compatibility inside this app. If a\nfirst version of a feature needs to change a few prompts later, do not layer\ncompatibility slop on top of it. Remove or replace the earlier approach when\nthat produces simpler, clearer code.\n\nIt is fine to throw out code that no longer matches the product direction. Smart\nagents can write better code than they can maintain a pile of special cases.\nPrefer one clean current path over preserving several historical paths.\n\n## Visual QA\n\nFor UI changes, reason through the actual states the player will see: active\nPokemon, benched Pokemon, hand cards, overflowing hands, prompt dialogs, hover,\nselected, disabled, face-down, and attached-card states.\n\nWatch especially for clipping, accidental shrinking, layout shifts, text\noverlap, mismatched scale between active and bench views, and shadows or glows\nbeing cut off by scroll containers.\n\n## Animation Development\n\nRead `docs/replay-animation-architecture.md` before touching animation code.\nThe short version: `choreograph()` in `src/lib/anim/motions.ts` is the single\nclassifier from timeline events to motions and target effects; the render\nlayers (`BoardAnimationLayer`, `ViewportAnimationLayer`, `RevealSessionLayer`)\nresolve anchors and execute; all animation-time hiding goes through\n`animVisibility` and the one `data-anim-hidden` attribute.\n\nRules that keep this system flicker-free:\n\n- One system animates a given event. New animation behavior goes into the\n  choreographer and an existing layer; do not add per-component event\n  classification, private hidden attributes, or component-local hide maps.\n- Sprites render from view data through `BoardSlot`/`CardTile`. Never clone\n  live DOM for a sprite, and never let an anchor query resolve inside a\n  `[data-anim-layer]` subtree.\n- When the final game state already contains the destination card, hide that\n  destination with a visibility claim only until handoff. When the final state\n  omits the source, use the pre-render snapshots (hand cards, attached badges)\n  rather than letting the source pop out early.\n- Timers belong to a layer, guarded by its generation counter, and are cleared\n  on scope changes and destroy. In replay, board-space sprites and claims hold\n  until the phase scope ends; the phase transition is the handoff. Do not\n  reveal old slots from inside a renderer.\n- Board-plane and viewport animations are different coordinate spaces. A card\n  that starts and ends on the tilted board stays inside the board plane\n  (offset-sum geometry); a card crossing between hand and board uses the\n  viewport layer and the homography in `planeGeometry.ts`.\n- Preserve the animation look. Keyframes, easings, and timing constants are\n  the product; change them deliberately, not as a refactor side effect.\n\n## Checks\n\nDo not run expensive checks reflexively after every small CSS tweak. Agents are\nexpected to reason carefully.\n\nRun `npm run build` and `npm test` for larger changes, behavior changes, shared\ncomponent changes, prompt-selection logic, game-state logic, or before committing\na meaningful batch. For very small visual-only edits, a targeted inspection is\noften enough.\n\n## Public Boundary\n\nDo not add Kaggle native binaries, raw competition bundles, or generated local\nmatch artifacts to this repo. Local CABT play should consume user-supplied\nresources through `CABT_SAMPLE_SUBMISSION_DIR`.\n","numLines":111,"startLine":1,"totalLines":111}},"sourceToolAssistantUUID":"1b5d6f3e-07dd-4902-8a5c-b7774eb6e3a2","sessionKind":"bg","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/charlielockyer/Documents/Code/ai-battle-challenge","sessionId":"6a7c23ff-6d4a-455f-bf85-fa444b0d588f","version":"2.1.205","gitBranch":"main"}

{"parentUuid":"8731de4f-8085-4d4d-93f0-d5ad7279b731","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"4efcb21a-f499-4ac1-955b-398653e0632c","agentId":"ab5a61a500485d254","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Qh5kaakvLhkNxxbzc1ZNTJ","type":"tool_result","content":"1\timport cardRows from './cardData.generated.json';\n2\timport attackRows from './attackData.generated.json';\n3\timport { CabtAreaType, CabtLogType } from './types';\n4\timport type { ActionTimelineEvent } from '../game/types';\n5\t\n6\ttype CardRow = {\n7\t  id: number;\n8\t  name: string;\n9\t  skills?: Array<{ name: string; text?: string }>;\n10\t};\n11\t\n12\ttype AttackRow = {\n13\t  attackId: number;\n14\t  name: string;\n15\t};\n16\t\n17\tconst cardDatabase = new Map<number, CardRow>((cardRows as CardRow[]).map((card) => [card.id, card]));\n18\tconst attackDatabase = new Map<number, AttackRow>((attackRows as AttackRow[]).map((attack) => [attack.attackId, attack]));\n19\t\n20\tconst logTypeNames: Record<number, string> = {\n21\t  [CabtLogType.SHUFFLE]: 'Shuffle',\n22\t  [CabtLogType.HAS_BASIC_POKEMON]: 'HasBasicPokemon',\n23\t  [CabtLogType.TURN_START]: 'TurnStart',\n24\t  [CabtLogType.TURN_END]: 'TurnEnd',\n25\t  [CabtLogType.DRAW]: 'Draw',\n26\t  [CabtLogType.DRAW_REVERSE]: 'DrawReverse',\n27\t  [CabtLogType.MOVE_CARD]: 'MoveCard',\n28\t  [CabtLogType.MOVE_CARD_REVERSE]: 'MoveCardReverse',\n29\t  [CabtLogType.SWITCH]: 'Switch',\n30\t  [CabtLogType.CHANGE]: 'Change',\n31\t  [CabtLogType.PLAY]: 'Play',\n32\t  [CabtLogType.ATTACH]: 'Attach',\n33\t  [CabtLogType.EVOLVE]: 'Evolve',\n34\t  [CabtLogType.DEVOLVE]: 'Devolve',\n35\t  [CabtLogType.MOVE_ATTACHED]: 'MoveAttached',\n36\t  [CabtLogType.ATTACK]: 'Attack',\n37\t  [CabtLogType.HP_CHANGE]: 'HPChange',\n38\t  [CabtLogType.POISONED]: 'Poisoned',\n39\t  [CabtLogType.BURNED]: 'Burned',\n40\t  [CabtLogType.ASLEEP]: 'Asleep',\n41\t  [CabtLogType.PARALYZED]: 'Paralyzed',\n42\t  [CabtLogType.CONFUSED]: 'Confused',\n43\t  [CabtLogType.COIN]: 'Coin',\n44\t  [CabtLogType.RESULT]: 'Result',\n45\t};\n46\t\n47\texport function formatCabtLog(log: Record<string, unknown>): string {\n48\t  const type = normalizedLogType(log.type);\n49\t  const playerIndex = typeof log.playerIndex === 'number' ? log.playerIndex : undefined;\n50\t  const actor = playerIndex === undefined ? 'Game' : `Player ${playerIndex + 1}`;\n51\t  const card = cardName(Number(log.cardId));\n52\t  const target = cardName(Number(log.cardIdTarget));\n53\t\n54\t  switch (type) {\n55\t    case 'Shuffle':\n56\t      return `${actor} shuffled their deck.`;\n57\t    case 'HasBasicPokemon':\n58\t      return `${actor} ${log.hasBasicPokemon ? 'has' : 'does not have'} a Basic Pokemon.`;\n59\t    case 'TurnStart':\n60\t      return `${actor} turn started.`;\n61\t    case 'TurnEnd':\n62\t      return `${actor} ended their turn.`;\n63\t    case 'Draw':\n64\t      return `${actor} drew ${card}.`;\n65\t    case 'DrawReverse':\n66\t      return `${actor} drew a card.`;\n67\t    case 'Play':\n68\t      return `${actor} played ${card}.`;\n69\t    case 'Attach':\n70\t      return `${actor} attached ${card}${Number.isFinite(Number(log.cardIdTarget)) ? ` to ${target}` : ''}.`;\n71\t    case 'Evolve':\n72\t      return `${actor} evolved into ${card}.`;\n73\t    case 'Devolve':\n74\t      return `${actor} devolved ${card}.`;\n75\t    case 'Attack':\n76\t      return `${actor} used ${attackName(Number(log.attackId))} with ${card}.`;\n77\t    case 'Ability': {\n78\t      const ability = abilityName(log);\n79\t      if (ability === 'Retreat') {\n80\t        return `${actor} retreated ${card}.`;\n81\t      }\n82\t      // Stadium effects: the \"ability\" IS the card, so \"with <card>\" is noise.\n83\t      return ability === card\n84\t        ? `${actor} used ${ability}.`\n85\t        : `${actor} used ${ability} with ${card}.`;\n86\t    }\n87\t    case 'MoveCard':\n88\t      return moveCardMessage(actor, card, log);\n89\t    case 'MoveCardReverse':\n90\t      return `${actor} moved a facedown card from ${areaName(log.fromArea)} to ${areaName(log.toArea)}.`;\n91\t    case 'Switch':\n92\t      return `${actor} switched ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdActive))} with ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdBench))}.`;\n93\t    case 'Change':\n94\t      return `${actor} changed ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdBefore))} into ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdAfter))}.`;\n95\t    case 'MoveAttached':\n96\t      return `${actor} moved ${card}.`;\n97\t    case 'HPChange':\n98\t      return hpChangeMessage(actor, card, log);\n99\t    case 'Poisoned':\n100\t      return `${actor}'s ${card} ${log.isRecover ? 'recovered from poison' : 'was poisoned'}.`;\n101\t    case 'Burned':\n102\t      return `${actor}'s ${card} ${log.isRecover ? 'recovered from burn' : 'was burned'}.`;\n103\t    case 'Asleep':\n104\t      return `${actor}'s ${card} ${log.isRecover ? 'woke up' : 'fell asleep'}.`;\n105\t    case 'Paralyzed':\n106\t      return `${actor}'s ${card} ${log.isRecover ? 'recovered from paralysis' : 'was paralyzed'}.`;\n107\t    case 'Confused':\n108\t      return `${actor}'s ${card} ${log.isRecover ? 'recovered from confusion' : 'was confused'}.`;\n109\t    case 'Coin':\n110\t      return `${actor} flipped ${log.head ? 'heads' : 'tails'}.`;\n111\t    case 'Result':\n112\t      return 'The battle finished.';\n113\t    default:\n114\t      return `${actor}: ${String(type ?? 'Event')}${Number.isFinite(Number(log.cardId)) ? ` ${card}` : ''}.`;\n115\t  }\n116\t}\n117\t\n118\texport function cabtLogsToTimeline(\n119\t  logs: Array<Record<string, unknown>>,\n120\t  options: { nextId?: number } = {},\n121\t): { events: ActionTimelineEvent[]; nextId: number } {\n122\t  let nextId = options.nextId ?? 1;\n123\t  const events = logs.map((log) => ({\n124\t    id: nextId++,\n125\t    message: formatCabtLog(log),\n126\t    playerIndex: typeof log.playerIndex === 'number' ? log.playerIndex : undefined,\n127\t    kind: normalizedLogType(log.type),\n128\t    params: log,\n129\t  }));\n130\t  return { events, nextId };\n131\t}\n132\t\n133\tfunction normalizedLogType(type: unknown): string {\n134\t  if (typeof type === 'number') {\n135\t    return logTypeNames[type] ?? `Log ${type}`;\n136\t  }\n137\t  return String(type ?? 'Event');\n138\t}\n139\t\n140\tfunction moveCardMessage(actor: string, card: string, log: Record<string, unknown>) {\n141\t  if (Number(log.fromArea) === CabtAreaType.PRIZE && Number(log.toArea) === CabtAreaType.HAND) {\n142\t    return `${actor} took ${card} as a Prize card.`;\n143\t  }\n144\t  if (Number(log.fromArea) === CabtAreaType.DECK && Number(log.toArea) === CabtAreaType.PRIZE) {\n145\t    return `${actor} set a Prize card.`;\n146\t  }\n147\t  if (Number(log.fromArea) === CabtAreaType.HAND && Number(log.toArea) === CabtAreaType.DECK) {\n148\t    return `${actor} moved a card from hand to deck.`;\n149\t  }\n150\t  if (Number(log.fromArea) === CabtAreaType.DECK && Number(log.toArea) === CabtAreaType.DISCARD) {\n151\t    return `${actor} discarded ${card} from the deck.`;\n152\t  }\n153\t  if (Number(log.toArea) === CabtAreaType.DECK_BOTTOM) {\n154\t    return `${actor} put ${card} on the bottom of the deck.`;\n155\t  }\n156\t  return `${actor} moved ${card} from ${areaName(log.fromArea)} to ${areaName(log.toArea)}.`;\n157\t}\n158\t\n159\tfunction hpChangeMessage(actor: string, card: string, log: Record<string, unknown>) {\n160\t  const value = Number(log.value);\n161\t  if (!Number.isFinite(value) || value === 0) {\n162\t    return `${actor}'s ${card} HP changed.`;\n163\t  }\n164\t  const amount = Math.abs(value);\n165\t  if (value < 0) {\n166\t    return `${actor}'s ${card} took ${amount} damage.`;\n167\t  }\n168\t  return `${actor}'s ${card} recovered ${amount} HP.`;\n169\t}\n170\t\n171\tfunction areaName(area: unknown): string {\n172\t  const areaMap: Record<number, string> = {\n173\t    [CabtAreaType.DECK]: 'deck',\n174\t    [CabtAreaType.HAND]: 'hand',\n175\t    [CabtAreaType.DISCARD]: 'discard',\n176\t    [CabtAreaType.ACTIVE]: 'active',\n177\t    [CabtAreaType.BENCH]: 'bench',\n178\t    [CabtAreaType.PRIZE]: 'prize',\n179\t    [CabtAreaType.STADIUM]: 'stadium',\n180\t    [CabtAreaType.ENERGY]: 'energy',\n181\t    [CabtAreaType.TOOL]: 'tool',\n182\t    [CabtAreaType.PRE_EVOLUTION]: 'evolution stack',\n183\t    [CabtAreaType.PLAYER]: 'player',\n184\t    [CabtAreaType.LOOKING]: 'Game' : `Player ${playerIndex + 1}`;\n  const card = cardName(Number(log.cardId));\n  const target = cardName(Number(log.cardIdTarget));\n\n  switch (type) {\n    case 'Shuffle':\n      return `${actor} shuffled their deck.`;\n    case 'HasBasicPokemon':\n      return `${actor} ${log.hasBasicPokemon ? 'has' : 'does not have'} a Basic Pokemon.`;\n    case 'TurnStart':\n      return `${actor} turn started.`;\n    case 'TurnEnd':\n      return `${actor} ended their turn.`;\n    case 'Draw':\n      return `${actor} drew ${card}.`;\n    case 'DrawReverse':\n      return `${actor} drew a card.`;\n    case 'Play':\n      return `${actor} played ${card}.`;\n    case 'Attach':\n      return `${actor} attached ${card}${Number.isFinite(Number(log.cardIdTarget)) ? ` to ${target}` : ''}.`;\n    case 'Evolve':\n      return `${actor} evolved into ${card}.`;\n    case 'Devolve':\n      return `${actor} devolved ${card}.`;\n    case 'Attack':\n      return `${actor} used ${attackName(Number(log.attackId))} with ${card}.`;\n    case 'Ability': {\n      const ability = abilityName(log);\n      if (ability === 'Retreat') {\n        return `${actor} retreated ${card}.`;\n      }\n      // Stadium effects: the \"ability\" IS the card, so \"with <card>\" is noise.\n      return ability === card\n        ? `${actor} used ${ability}.`\n        : `${actor} used ${ability} with ${card}.`;\n    }\n    case 'MoveCard':\n      return moveCardMessage(actor, card, log);\n    case 'MoveCardReverse':\n      return `${actor} moved a facedown card from ${areaName(log.fromArea)} to ${areaName(log.toArea)}.`;\n    case 'Switch':\n      return `${actor} switched ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdActive))} with ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdBench))}.`;\n    case 'Change':\n      return `${actor} changed ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdBefore))} into ${cardName(Number(log.cardIdAfter))}.`;\n    case 'MoveAttached':\n      return `${actor} moved ${card}.`;\n    case 'HPChange':\n      return hpChangeMessage(actor, card, log);\n    case 'Poisoned':\n      return `${actor}'s ${card} ${log.isRecover ? 'recovered from paralysis' : 'was paralyzed'}.`;\n    case 'Confused':\n      return `${actor}'s ${card} ${log.isRecover ? 'recovered from confusion' : 'was confused'}.`;\n    case 'Coin':\n      return `${actor} flipped ${log.head ? 'heads' : 'tails'}.`;\n    case 'Result':\n      return 'The battle finished.';\n    default:\n      return `${actor}: ${String(type ?? 'Event');\n}\n\nfunction moveCardMessage(actor: string, card: string, log: Record<string, unknown>) {\n  if (Number(log.fromArea) === CabtAreaType.PRIZE && Number(log.toArea) === CabtAreaType.HAND) {\n    return `${actor} took ${card} as a Prize card.`;\n  }\n  if (Number(log.fromArea) === CabtAreaType.DECK && Number(log.toArea) === CabtAreaType.PRIZE) {\n    return `${actor} set a Prize return `${actor} put ${card} on the bottom of the deck.`;\n  }\n  return `${actor} moved ${card} from ${areaName(log.fromArea)} to ${areaName(log.toArea)}.`;\n}\n\nfunction hpChangeMessage(actor: string, card: string, log: Record<string, unknown>) {\n  const value = Number(log.value);\n  if (!Number.isFinite(value) || value === 0) {\n    return `${actor}'s ${card} HP changed.`;\n  }\n  const amount = Math.abs(value);\n  if (value < 0) {\n    return `${actor}'s ${card} took ${amount} damage.`;\n  }\n  return `${actor}'s ${card} recovered ${amount} HP.`;\n}\n\nfunction areaName(area: unknown): string {\n  const areaMap: Record<number, string> = {\n    [CabtAreaType.DECK]: 'deck',\n    [CabtAreaType.HAND]: 'hand',\n    [CabtAreaType.DISCARD]: 'discard',\n    [CabtAreaType.ACTIVE]: [CabtAreaType.DECK_BOTTOM]: 'the bottom of the deck',\n  };\n  return areaMap[Number(area)] ?? 'Event');\n}\n\nfunction numberField(value: unknown): number | undefined {\n  const number = Number(value);\n  return Number.isFinite(number) ? number : undefined;\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Decision-based step splitting.\n//\n// A replay step is one root decision and everything it caused. The frame\n// stream records decisions directly: each frame's `action` answers the\n// previous frame's `select`. A select offering an End option is the main\n// action menu, so a frame that answers it starts a new step (play, attach,\n// evolve, ability, attack, retreat, end turn). Any other select is a\n// sub-decision whose consequences belong to the current step, and a frame\n// without a select is engine auto-resolution that also continues the current\n// step. Forced transitions (turn end/start, checkup, result) always cut, even\n// mid-frame. Naming drift + markers\n\n- **`HpChange` vs `HPChange` — real, and it is not arbitrary drift, it's two live upstream spellings.** The bridge's own log-type table (`logFormat.ts:37`) canonically emits `'HPChange'` for `CabtLogType.HP_CHANGE`; the Kaggle-recorded replay JSON's raw `log.type` string field literally arrives as `'HpChange'` (mixed case) and is passed through unchanged by `normalizedFrameLogType` (`cabtReplay.ts:553-555`, a bare `String(type)`). Both spellings are genuinely live (one per data source), so this isn't a fossil of dead code — but the `event.kind === 'HpChange' || event.kind === 'HPChange'` guard is copy-pasted at 6+ sites instead of normalized once at ingestion: `motions.ts:175`, `timing.ts:109`, `cabtReplay.ts:1453,2128,2651-2652`, `actionAnimationCoverage.ts:206`. **WORTH-A-SLICE** — canonicalize to one spelling inside `cabtReplay.ts`'s frame-ingestion step (where `normalizedFrameLogType` already lives) so every downstream consumer only ever sees one string.\n- **`knock-out` (motion style literal) vs `KnockOut` (phase-key prefix) vs `knockOut`/`isKnockOutMove`/`isKnockOutEvent` (function names)** — this is consistent, intentional casing-by-role (CSS-ish kebab literal for the motion style enum, PascalCase for phase-key namespacing, camelCase for functions), not drift. **N/A — do not re-file.**\n- `TODO`/`FIXME`/`HACK`/`XXX`: **zero hits anywhere in `src/`.**\n- `@ts-ignore`/`@ts-expect-error`: **zero hits.**\n- `eslint-disable`: **exactly one**, `src/probes/wholeGameSwapInertness.probe.dom.test.ts:263`, disabling `no-console` for the probe's own intentional diagnostic printout — fully justified, not debt.\n\nThis codebase is unusually clean on markers; the \"debt\" here is structural/duplication, not marker-flagged shortcuts.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Fossil compatibility shims\n\n- **`HpChange`/`HPChange` dual-spelling checks** (also listed in §6) are the clearest fossil-shim-shaped pattern in the repo, though as noted it's driven by two genuinely-live data sources, not a deleted format. Rated **WORTH-A-SLICE** to consolidate at the boundary rather than at every consumer.\n- **`type === CabtOptionType.END || type === 'End'`** and **`optionType !== 'Yes' && optionType !== CabtOptionType.YES'`** (`cabtReplay.ts:844,251`) — tolerant parsing for older Kaggle-recorded JSON that may predate a string→enum refactor of `option.type`. Real, narrow, already has an unused normalizer (`normalizedOptionType`) sitting right next to it that should absorb both. **TRIVIAL/WORTH-A-SLICE**, same item as §2.\n- Anchor fallback chains (`anchors.ts`) and prizeSourceRects/takeIndex extrapolation were explicitly praised as *correct design* by the prior audits (\"the design is right; live's problems are missing data, not the resolver\") — I re-checked and concur; these are legitimate multi-source-of-truth fallbacks for a system with partial information, not \"just in case\" fossils. **N/A — do not re-file.**\n- No other tolerant-parser-for-a-format-that-no-longer-occurs pattern found.
